Sub-objective: 1.1 — Given a scenario, install and configure laptop hardware and components
Question: A technician is asked to install a solid-state drive in a legacy laptop that has only a standard 2.5-inch HDD bay. The buyer purchased an mSATA SSD by mistake. What should the technician recommend?
A) Use an mSATA to 2.5-inch SATA adapter to mount the mSATA SSD in the HDD bay
B) Install the mSATA SSD directly in the HDD bay using double-sided tape
C) Return the mSATA SSD and purchase a 2.5-inch SATA SSD instead
D) Use an M.2 to 2.5-inch adapter since mSATA and M.2 are the same
Correct: C
Explanation: An mSATA SSD requires an mSATA slot (a mini-PCIe-style connector); it cannot be directly installed in a 2.5-inch HDD bay. While mSATA-to-2.5-inch adapters exist (option A is technically possible), for most field scenarios the simplest and most reliable solution is to exchange for the correct drive type — a standard 2.5-inch SATA SSD. mSATA and M.2 are different standards with different connectors and are not interchangeable without an adapter.

Domain: 1.0 Mobile Devices
Sub-objective: 1.4 — Given a scenario, configure basic mobile-device network connectivity and application support
Question: A user wants to configure their mobile email for a Google Workspace account using IMAP. What is the correct incoming mail server hostname?
A) pop.google.com
B) smtp.gmail.com
C) imap.gmail.com
D) exchange.google.com
Correct: C
Explanation: Google's IMAP incoming mail server is imap.gmail.com (port 993, SSL); this is the standard hostname used for configuring Gmail in third-party email clients on mobile devices. smtp.gmail.com is the outgoing mail server for sending. pop.google.com does not exist — Google's POP3 server is pop.gmail.com. Google does not operate an Exchange server.

Domain: 1.0 Mobile Devices
Sub-objective: 1.2 — Compare and contrast display components of mobile devices
Question: A high-end laptop advertises a display with a 10-bit colour depth. What advantage does this provide over a standard 8-bit display?
A) The display refreshes faster, reducing motion blur
B) The display can produce over 1 billion colours versus 16.7 million, enabling smoother colour gradients
C) The display uses less power because fewer colours are rendered
D) The display resolution is four times higher than 8-bit panels
Correct: B
Explanation: 8-bit panels can display 256 shades per RGB channel (2^8 x 3 = 16.7 million colours), while 10-bit panels provide 1,024 shades per channel (2^10 x 3 = over 1 billion colours), resulting in smoother colour gradients with no visible banding — important for professional photo and video work. Colour bit depth is independent of refresh rate, power consumption, and resolution.

Domain: 1.0 Mobile Devices
Sub-objective: 1.3 — Given a scenario, set up and configure accessories and ports of mobile devices
Question: A user's laptop has a port with a small symbol resembling a trident (three-pronged). What port type does this symbol represent?
A) USB Type-A
B) Thunderbolt
C) HDMI
D) eSATA
Correct: B
Explanation: The Thunderbolt interface is identified by a lightning bolt or, specifically on Thunderbolt 1 and 2, a symbol resembling a lightning bolt with a thunderbolt, sometimes colloquially called a trident; Thunderbolt 3 and 4 share the USB-C physical connector but are still identified by the lightning bolt icon. USB Type-A has a standard rectangular connector with no special symbol on the port. HDMI uses the HDMI logo and eSATA uses an eSATA symbol on its port.

Domain: 1.0 Mobile Devices
Sub-objective: 1.1 — Given a scenario, install and configure laptop hardware and components
Question: During a RAM upgrade, a technician installs a DDR5 SO-DIMM into a DDR4 laptop. The laptop will not POST. What is the most likely reason?
A) The DDR5 module needs to be configured in the BIOS before it will operate
B) DDR5 and DDR4 SO-DIMMs are physically incompatible — the notch positions differ, preventing incorrect insertion
C) The DDR5 module requires a higher voltage that damaged the motherboard
D) DDR5 requires dual-channel configuration to POST
Correct: B
Explanation: DDR5 SO-DIMMs have a notch in a different position than DDR4 SO-DIMMs to prevent physical insertion into incompatible slots; in most cases the DDR5 module simply cannot be fully seated in a DDR4 slot. If forced, it would not POST or could damage the slot. No BIOS configuration can bridge the generational hardware incompatibility between DDR4 and DDR5.

Domain: 1.0 Mobile Devices
Sub-objective: 1.4 — Given a scenario, configure basic mobile-device network connectivity and application support
Question: A hospital requires that patient data on employee smartphones be inaccessible if the device is left idle for more than 5 minutes. Which MDM policy enforces this?
A) Remote wipe after idle timeout
B) Screen lock / auto-lock timeout policy with passcode enforcement
C) Geofencing restriction
D) Application sandboxing policy
Correct: B
Explanation: An MDM screen lock / auto-lock timeout policy forces the device to lock after a specified period of inactivity and requires a passcode or biometric to unlock, protecting sensitive data from unauthorised access if the device is left unattended. Remote wipe deletes data but does not restrict access after a short idle period. Geofencing restricts or enables features based on location, not idle time.

Domain: 1.0 Mobile Devices
Sub-objective: 1.3 — Given a scenario, set up and configure accessories and ports of mobile devices
Question: A technician configures a laptop to accept connections from a USB 3.0 flash drive. The flash drive is inserted but Windows reports a "USB device not recognised" error. What should the technician check first?
A) Whether NFC is enabled on the laptop
B) Whether the USB port is disabled in the BIOS or the USB controller driver needs to be reinstalled
C) Whether the flash drive needs to be formatted with NTFS using Disk Management
D) Whether the user's MDM profile blocks all USB storage
Correct: B
Explanation: "USB device not recognised" commonly indicates a driver issue with the USB host controller or the device itself; the technician should verify the USB controller is enabled in BIOS and that the controller driver is installed correctly in Device Manager. If MDM is blocking USB storage (option D), the error would typically be "access denied" or the device would appear as blocked, not "not recognised." NFC has no relationship to USB device recognition.

Domain: 1.0 Mobile Devices
Sub-objective: 1.2 — Compare and contrast display components of mobile devices
Question: A laptop screen is cracked and the user observes black spreading ink-like patches across the display. What physical component is damaged?
A) The digitizer layer
B) The LCD panel's liquid crystal layer (broken LCD)
C) The LED backlight strip
D) The display inverter
Correct: B
Explanation: The spreading black "ink" pattern is liquid crystal fluid leaking from the broken cells within the LCD matrix after the panel is cracked; this damage is irreversible and requires full panel replacement. The digitizer is a transparent capacitive layer that does not produce visible colour — its damage would not cause spreading discolouration. Backlight failure causes dimness or complete darkness, not ink-like spreading patches.

Domain: 1.0 Mobile Devices
Sub-objective: 1.4 — Given a scenario, configure basic mobile-device network connectivity and application support
Question: A user travelling internationally wants to avoid roaming charges but still use data apps on their smartphone. What is the simplest option using the device's built-in features?
A) Enable VPN to route data through the home country
B) Purchase and insert a local SIM card, or use an eSIM with a local carrier profile
C) Enable Bluetooth tethering from a second phone
D) Configure the device to use Wi-Fi calling only and disable all data
Correct: B
Explanation: Installing a local SIM card (or activating a local eSIM profile on supported devices) gives the phone a local number and data plan at local rates, eliminating international roaming charges while providing full data access. A VPN routes traffic securely but does not eliminate roaming data charges — the cellular carrier still bills for international data use. Disabling all data (option D) would prevent internet use, which is the opposite of what the user wants.

Domain: 1.0 Mobile Devices
Sub-objective: 1.1 — Given a scenario, install and configure laptop hardware and components
Question: A user reports that after cleaning their laptop's keyboard, several keys are sticking and not registering presses. The keyboard was cleaned with a wet cloth while the laptop was powered on. What is the most likely cause, and what should be done?
A) The keyboard driver became corrupted; reinstall the driver
B) Moisture entered the keyboard membrane or keyswitches; power off immediately and allow the keyboard to dry fully before reuse
C) The keyboard backlight intensity was changed during cleaning
D) The ZIF connector loosened during cleaning; reseat it
Correct: B
Explanation: Cleaning electronics with a wet cloth while powered on introduces moisture into the keyboard mechanism, causing keys to stick, miss presses, or short out; the safest immediate action is to power off and remove the battery if possible, then allow complete drying (often 24–48 hours) before powering on again. Keyboard driver corruption would cause keys to not register but would not cause physical sticking. Keyboard backlight changes are a software/settings issue unrelated to physical sticking.
Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast TCP and UDP ports, protocols, and their purposes
Question: Which port number does FTP use to transfer data between a client and server?
A) 20
B) 21
C) 22
D) 23
Correct: A
Explanation: FTP uses two ports: port 21 for control (commands) and port 20 for active data transfer. The control connection on port 21 establishes the session and sends commands, while the actual file data travels over port 20 in active mode. Passive mode FTP uses ephemeral ports for data but still uses port 21 for control.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast TCP and UDP ports, protocols, and their purposes
Question: A technician needs to securely manage a remote Linux server from the command line. Which protocol and port should they use?
A) Telnet on port 23
B) RDP on port 3389
C) SSH on port 22
D) FTP on port 21
Correct: C
Explanation: SSH (Secure Shell) operates on port 22 and provides encrypted command-line access to remote systems. Telnet on port 23 provides similar functionality but transmits all data, including credentials, in plaintext. SSH has largely replaced Telnet in professional environments because of its strong encryption and authentication options.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast TCP and UDP ports, protocols, and their purposes
Question: Which protocol is responsible for dynamically assigning IP addresses to client devices, and which ports does it use?
A) DNS using ports 53 UDP and TCP
B) DHCP using ports 67 and 68
C) LDAP using port 389
D) SMTP using port 25
Correct: B
Explanation: DHCP (Dynamic Host Configuration Protocol) uses port 67 on the server side to receive client requests and port 68 on the client side to receive responses. It operates over UDP because the four-step DORA process (Discover, Offer, Request, Acknowledge) requires broadcast communication before a client has an IP address. DNS uses port 53, not DHCP's ports.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast TCP and UDP ports, protocols, and their purposes
Question: A user complains they can receive emails but cannot send them. The help desk determines outbound SMTP is blocked. Which port is most likely being filtered by the ISP?
A) 110
B) 143
C) 25
D) 443
Correct: C
Explanation: SMTP uses port 25 for server-to-server mail transfer, and many ISPs block outbound port 25 to prevent spam from compromised client machines. Port 110 is POP3 (incoming mail retrieval) and port 143 is IMAP (incoming mail retrieval with folder sync). The user should configure their email client to use port 587 (SMTP with TLS) for authenticated outbound mail submission.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast TCP and UDP ports, protocols, and their purposes
Question: Which port does HTTPS use to provide encrypted web browsing?
A) 80
B) 8080
C) 443
D) 3389
Correct: C
Explanation: HTTPS (HTTP Secure) operates on port 443 and uses TLS to encrypt web traffic between the browser and the server. Standard HTTP uses port 80 and sends data in plaintext, making it vulnerable to interception. Port 8080 is a common alternative HTTP port used in proxy and development environments, while 3389 is RDP.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast TCP and UDP ports, protocols, and their purposes
Question: DNS queries are typically sent using which transport protocol and port?
A) TCP port 53
B) UDP port 53
C) UDP port 67
D) TCP port 443
Correct: B
Explanation: The vast majority of DNS queries use UDP on port 53 because the small query and response sizes fit within a single packet, and the speed of UDP is preferable for frequent lookups. DNS falls back to TCP on port 53 for responses larger than 512 bytes and for zone transfers between DNS servers. Both TCP and UDP port 53 are technically used by DNS, but UDP is the default for standard queries.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast TCP and UDP ports, protocols, and their purposes
Question: A user wants to access their email and keep messages synchronized across multiple devices with folder support. Which protocol should their email client be configured to use?
A) SMTP on port 25
B) POP3 on port 110
C) IMAP on port 143
D) LDAP on port 389
Correct: C
Explanation: IMAP (Internet Message Access Protocol) on port 143 keeps mail stored on the server and synchronizes folder structure and read status across all connected devices. POP3 on port 110 downloads messages to a single device and typically deletes them from the server, making multi-device access difficult. SMTP on port 25 handles outgoing mail, not retrieval.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast TCP and UDP ports, protocols, and their purposes
Question: A corporate environment uses Windows file shares that are accessible over the network. Which port must be open to allow SMB/CIFS traffic?
A) 139
B) 389
C) 445
D) 636
Correct: C
Explanation: SMB (Server Message Block), also known as CIFS, uses port 445 for direct TCP connections to Windows file and printer shares over modern networks. Port 139 was used by the older NetBIOS Session Service for SMB over NetBIOS, but modern Windows networks use port 445 directly. Ports 389 and 636 are used by LDAP and LDAPS for directory services.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast TCP and UDP ports, protocols, and their purposes
Question: A mail server administrator needs to configure clients to submit outgoing mail with authentication and encryption. Which port should be used?
A) 25
B) 110
C) 465
D) 587
Correct: D
Explanation: Port 587 is the designated mail submission port for authenticated SMTP with STARTTLS encryption, as defined by RFC 6409. Port 25 is used for server-to-server (MTA-to-MTA) mail relay and is often blocked by ISPs for client use to prevent spam. Port 110 is POP3, and while port 465 was historically used for SMTPS, port 587 is the current standard for authenticated submission.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast TCP and UDP ports, protocols, and their purposes
Question: Which protocol and port does a technician use to connect to a Windows remote desktop session?
A) SSH on port 22
B) VNC on port 5900
C) RDP on port 3389
D) Telnet on port 23
Correct: C
Explanation: RDP (Remote Desktop Protocol) uses port 3389 and is Microsoft's built-in protocol for graphical remote desktop access to Windows systems. SSH on port 22 provides encrypted command-line access and is more common in Linux/Unix environments. VNC on port 5900 is a cross-platform graphical remote access protocol but is not built into Windows by default.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast TCP and UDP ports, protocols, and their purposes
Question: LDAP is used for querying directory services. Which port does standard (unencrypted) LDAP use?
A) 389
B) 443
C) 636
D) 3268
Correct: A
Explanation: LDAP (Lightweight Directory Access Protocol) uses port 389 for standard unencrypted or STARTTLS-upgraded connections to directory services like Active Directory. LDAPS (LDAP over SSL/TLS) uses port 636 for encrypted connections. Port 443 is HTTPS and port 3268 is used for Active Directory Global Catalog queries.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast TCP and UDP ports, protocols, and their purposes
Question: A technician is setting up a legacy system that requires unencrypted remote terminal access. Which protocol operates on port 23?
A) SSH
B) FTP
C) Telnet
D) TFTP
Correct: C
Explanation: Telnet operates on port 23 and provides unencrypted terminal access to remote devices. It transmits all data including usernames and passwords in plaintext, making it a security risk on modern networks. SSH on port 22 is the secure replacement for Telnet and should be used whenever possible.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast TCP and UDP ports, protocols, and their purposes
Question: Which of the following correctly pairs a protocol with its primary function and port?
A) IMAP / 110 — download mail to single device
B) SMTP / 587 — authenticated mail submission with encryption
C) POP3 / 143 — synchronise mail across multiple devices
D) DNS / 68 — resolve hostnames to IP addresses
Correct: B
Explanation: SMTP on port 587 is the correct port for authenticated mail submission using STARTTLS encryption, which is what modern email clients use to send outgoing mail. IMAP uses port 143 (not 110), and POP3 uses port 110 (not 143). DNS uses port 53, not port 68; port 68 is the DHCP client port.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast TCP and UDP ports, protocols, and their purposes
Question: A company deploys a secure directory service using SSL/TLS encryption. Which port should be used for LDAPS?
A) 389
B) 443
C) 636
D) 990
Correct: C
Explanation: LDAPS (LDAP Secure) uses port 636 to wrap LDAP traffic inside an SSL/TLS tunnel from the start of the connection. Standard LDAP on port 389 can also be upgraded with STARTTLS, but LDAPS on port 636 establishes the encrypted channel before any directory data is exchanged. Port 443 is HTTPS and port 990 is FTPS.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast TCP and UDP ports, protocols, and their purposes
Question: A network administrator needs to configure a router to allow web browsing. Which port must be permitted for standard HTTP traffic?
A) 21
B) 23
C) 80
D) 8443
Correct: C
Explanation: HTTP (Hypertext Transfer Protocol) uses port 80 for unencrypted web traffic. Port 21 is FTP control, port 23 is Telnet, and port 8443 is an alternative HTTPS port sometimes used by web applications. Firewalls and ACLs must allow outbound TCP connections to port 80 to permit standard web browsing.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast common networking hardware
Question: A technician needs to connect multiple devices on a LAN so that traffic from one device is sent only to the intended destination device. Which device should be deployed?
A) Hub
B) Switch
C) Repeater
D) Bridge
Correct: B
Explanation: A managed or unmanaged switch uses MAC address tables to forward frames only to the port where the destination device resides, reducing unnecessary traffic on the network. A hub broadcasts all incoming traffic out every port regardless of destination, wasting bandwidth and creating collisions. Switches operate at OSI Layer 2 and are the standard device for modern LAN connectivity.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast common networking hardware
Question: Which device is responsible for directing traffic between different IP networks and determining the best path for data packets?
A) Switch
B) Hub
C) Router
D) Access Point
Correct: C
Explanation: A router operates at OSI Layer 3 and uses IP routing tables to forward packets between different networks, including connecting a LAN to the internet. Switches operate at Layer 2 and forward frames within the same network segment using MAC addresses. Hubs are Layer 1 devices that simply repeat signals to all connected ports without any intelligence.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast common networking hardware
Question: A SOHO network needs to provide Wi-Fi connectivity to wireless clients while connecting to an existing wired switch infrastructure. Which device should be deployed?
A) Modem
B) Patch panel
C) Wireless Access Point
D) PoE switch
Correct: C
Explanation: A Wireless Access Point (WAP or AP) provides 802.11 Wi-Fi connectivity for wireless clients and bridges wireless traffic to the wired network. A modem converts signals between the ISP's medium and the local network but does not provide wireless client access on its own. A patch panel organises cabling but provides no active network functionality.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast common networking hardware
Question: What is the primary function of a patch panel in a structured cabling installation?
A) Amplify network signals over long cable runs
B) Provide a central termination point for horizontal cabling runs
C) Route traffic between VLANs
D) Convert digital signals to analog for DSL transmission
Correct: B
Explanation: A patch panel provides a fixed, organised termination point for horizontal cable runs from wall jacks, allowing flexible connections to switches via short patch cables. This makes moves, adds, and changes easier without disturbing the permanent cabling infrastructure. Patch panels are passive devices — they provide no amplification, routing, or signal conversion.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast common networking hardware
Question: A company wants to power IP phones and wireless access points without running separate electrical cables to each device. Which technology enables this?
A) ONT
B) SDN
C) Power over Ethernet (PoE)
D) Cable modem
Correct: C
Explanation: Power over Ethernet (PoE) delivers electrical power alongside data over standard Ethernet cables, eliminating the need for separate power supplies for devices like IP phones, cameras, and wireless APs. IEEE 802.3af provides up to 15.4W per port, while 802.3at (PoE+) provides up to 30W. The PoE switch or injector supplies the power, and the powered device (PD) receives it.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast common networking hardware
Question: Which device converts the signal from a fiber optic line from an ISP into an Ethernet connection usable by a home router?
A) Cable modem
B) DSL modem
C) Optical Network Terminal (ONT)
D) Wireless access point
Correct: C
Explanation: An ONT (Optical Network Terminal) is the customer-premises device that terminates a fiber optic connection from the ISP's network and converts the optical signal to an electrical Ethernet signal. A cable modem converts DOCSIS signals from coaxial cable, while a DSL modem works over telephone lines. The ONT is typical in FTTH (Fiber to the Home) deployments.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast common networking hardware
Question: A network administrator wants to implement software-defined networking to centralise control of network devices. Which component is central to SDN architecture?
A) Hub
B) SDN controller
C) Patch panel
D) Unmanaged switch
Correct: B
Explanation: In SDN (Software-Defined Networking), a centralised SDN controller separates the control plane from the data plane, allowing network behaviour to be programmatically managed rather than configured device by device. Network devices in an SDN environment become simple forwarding elements that receive instructions from the controller. This architecture enables rapid policy changes and automated network management across the entire infrastructure.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast common networking hardware
Question: A technician notices that a legacy hub is causing performance problems because all devices share the same collision domain. Which replacement device would create individual collision domains for each connected device?
A) Repeater
B) Bridge
C) Switch
D) Passive splitter
Correct: C
Explanation: A switch places each port in its own collision domain, so devices can transmit simultaneously without collisions using full-duplex communication. A hub places all connected devices in a single collision domain, so only one device can transmit at a time using CSMA/CD. A repeater and bridge also reduce collision domains but a switch is the correct modern replacement that provides per-port isolation.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast common networking hardware
Question: Which device is used to connect a LAN to the internet via a cable TV infrastructure using the DOCSIS standard?
A) DSL modem
B) ONT
C) Cable modem
D) Satellite modem
Correct: C
Explanation: A cable modem uses the DOCSIS (Data Over Cable Service Interface Specification) standard to transmit data over coaxial cable television infrastructure. DSL modems use telephone lines (twisted pair) via ADSL or VDSL standards. An ONT is used for fiber optic connections, not cable TV coax.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast common networking hardware
Question: A firewall is positioned at the network perimeter. Which primary function does it serve?
A) Assign IP addresses to client devices dynamically
B) Amplify Wi-Fi signals for extended coverage
C) Inspect and filter traffic based on security rules
D) Convert hostnames to IP addresses
Correct: C
Explanation: A firewall inspects network traffic and enforces security policies by permitting or denying packets based on rules related to IP addresses, ports, and protocols. Modern stateful firewalls also track connection state to make more intelligent filtering decisions. IP address assignment is DHCP's role, hostname resolution is DNS's role, and Wi-Fi amplification is done by range extenders or APs.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast common networking hardware
Question: A technician must install a NIC in a desktop PC to enable wired network connectivity. At which OSI layer does a NIC primarily operate?
A) Layer 1 — Physical
B) Layer 2 — Data Link
C) Layer 3 — Network
D) Layer 4 — Transport
Correct: B
Explanation: A NIC (Network Interface Card) operates at OSI Layer 2 (Data Link), using a unique burned-in MAC address for frame-level identification and communication. It also interfaces with Layer 1 physical media (copper or fiber) to transmit and receive electrical or optical signals. The NIC does not make routing decisions (Layer 3) or manage connections (Layer 4).

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Compare and contrast protocols for wireless networking
Question: Which IEEE 802.11 standard introduced Wi-Fi 6 and operates on both 2.4 GHz and 5 GHz bands with OFDMA technology?
A) 802.11ac
B) 802.11n
C) 802.11ax
D) 802.11g
Correct: C
Explanation: 802.11ax, marketed as Wi-Fi 6, introduced OFDMA (Orthogonal Frequency Division Multiple Access) to improve efficiency in dense environments with many simultaneous clients. It operates on both 2.4 GHz and 5 GHz and significantly increases throughput and reduces latency compared to its predecessor 802.11ac (Wi-Fi 5). Wi-Fi 6E extends 802.11ax to the 6 GHz band as well.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Compare and contrast protocols for wireless networking
Question: A wireless AP is configured to use the 2.4 GHz band. What is one major advantage of the 2.4 GHz band over 5 GHz?
A) Higher maximum throughput
B) Less interference from neighbouring networks
C) Greater range and better wall penetration
D) More non-overlapping channels
Correct: C
Explanation: The 2.4 GHz band has longer wavelengths that penetrate walls and obstacles more effectively and travel greater distances than 5 GHz signals. However, 2.4 GHz is more congested because it is used by many devices including microwaves, baby monitors, and Bluetooth. The 5 GHz band offers more non-overlapping channels and higher throughput but with reduced range.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Compare and contrast protocols for wireless networking
Question: Which 802.11 standard was the first to support operation exclusively on the 5 GHz band, offering speeds up to 54 Mbps?
A) 802.11b
B) 802.11g
C) 802.11a
D) 802.11n
Correct: C
Explanation: 802.11a was released simultaneously with 802.11b and operated exclusively in the 5 GHz band with a maximum data rate of 54 Mbps. Because it operated at 5 GHz, it avoided interference from 2.4 GHz devices but had reduced range compared to 802.11b. 802.11g brought 54 Mbps to the 2.4 GHz band and was backward compatible with 802.11b.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Compare and contrast protocols for wireless networking
Question: A technician is troubleshooting interference on a 2.4 GHz wireless network with multiple neighbouring APs. Which channels should be used to avoid overlap?
A) Channels 1, 5, and 9
B) Channels 1, 6, and 11
C) Channels 2, 7, and 12
D) Channels 1, 4, and 8
Correct: B
Explanation: In the 2.4 GHz band, channels 1, 6, and 11 are the only three non-overlapping channels in North America (each 22 MHz wide with 5 MHz spacing requires channels separated by at least 5 channels to avoid overlap). Using overlapping channels causes co-channel interference that degrades performance for all affected networks. The 5 GHz band has many more non-overlapping channels, making channel planning easier.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Compare and contrast protocols for wireless networking
Question: Which wireless standard introduced MIMO (Multiple-Input Multiple-Output) and dual-band operation on both 2.4 GHz and 5 GHz?
A) 802.11g
B) 802.11a
C) 802.11n
D) 802.11ac
Correct: C
Explanation: 802.11n (Wi-Fi 4) introduced MIMO technology, which uses multiple antennas to transmit and receive multiple data streams simultaneously, significantly increasing throughput. It was also the first standard to support dual-band operation on both 2.4 GHz and 5 GHz. 802.11ac (Wi-Fi 5) extended MIMO with MU-MIMO on the 5 GHz band.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Compare and contrast protocols for wireless networking
Question: Bluetooth is commonly used for short-range personal area network connections. In which frequency band does Bluetooth operate?
A) 900 MHz
B) 2.4 GHz
C) 5 GHz
D) 60 GHz
Correct: B
Explanation: Bluetooth operates in the 2.4 GHz ISM (Industrial, Scientific, and Medical) band, the same band used by 802.11b/g/n wireless networks, which can cause interference between the two technologies. Bluetooth uses frequency-hopping spread spectrum (FHSS) to minimise interference by rapidly changing frequencies. Its range is typically up to 10 metres for Class 2 devices and up to 100 metres for Class 1 devices.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Compare and contrast protocols for wireless networking
Question: A retail store wants to implement a system for contactless payment using smartphones tapped to a payment terminal. Which wireless technology is most appropriate?
A) Bluetooth
B) Zigbee
C) NFC
D) Z-Wave
Correct: C
Explanation: NFC (Near Field Communication) operates at 13.56 MHz and is designed for very short-range communication (typically less than 4 cm), making it ideal for contactless payments, access badges, and device pairing. Bluetooth operates at up to 10-100 metres range and requires device pairing. Zigbee and Z-Wave are mesh networking protocols designed for IoT and home automation devices.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Compare and contrast protocols for wireless networking
Question: A smart home system uses a mesh protocol operating at 908 MHz (US) for connecting light switches, door locks, and thermostats. Which technology is being described?
A) Zigbee
B) Z-Wave
C) NFC
D) Bluetooth LE
Correct: B
Explanation: Z-Wave is a wireless mesh protocol designed for home automation that operates at 908.42 MHz in the US (868 MHz in Europe), which is below the 2.4 GHz band and thus avoids interference with Wi-Fi and Bluetooth. It supports mesh networking where devices relay signals, extending range throughout a home. Zigbee operates at 2.4 GHz and is a competing home automation standard.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Compare and contrast protocols for wireless networking
Question: Which wireless standard operates exclusively on the 5 GHz band and introduced MU-MIMO and beamforming for maximum theoretical speeds of nearly 7 Gbps?
A) 802.11n
B) 802.11g
C) 802.11ac
D) 802.11ax
Correct: C
Explanation: 802.11ac (Wi-Fi 5) operates exclusively on the 5 GHz band and introduced downlink MU-MIMO (Multi-User MIMO), allowing an AP to transmit to multiple clients simultaneously, along with beamforming to focus the signal toward specific clients. Maximum theoretical throughput on 802.11ac wave 2 reaches approximately 6.9 Gbps with 160 MHz channels and 8x8 MU-MIMO. 802.11ax (Wi-Fi 6) subsequently improved on this with OFDMA on both bands.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Compare and contrast protocols for wireless networking
Question: A company deploys a fixed wireless internet link between two buildings 3 km apart using directional antennas. Which category of wireless technology best describes this solution?
A) WLAN
B) PAN
C) Long-range fixed wireless
D) Bluetooth
Correct: C
Explanation: Long-range fixed wireless uses directional (point-to-point) antennas to create dedicated wireless links between fixed locations over distances from hundreds of metres to many kilometres. This is commonly used to connect buildings where laying physical cable is impractical or expensive. WLAN refers to local Wi-Fi networks, PAN covers personal area networks like Bluetooth, and both operate at much shorter ranges.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Compare and contrast protocols for wireless networking
Question: Which generation of cellular technology introduced the first truly broadband mobile data experience with LTE?
A) 3G
B) 4G
C) 5G
D) 2G
Correct: B
Explanation: 4G LTE (Long Term Evolution) delivered mobile broadband speeds typically in the range of 10-100 Mbps, enabling streaming video, video calling, and cloud applications on mobile devices. 3G introduced mobile data but at much slower speeds (typically under 10 Mbps) with technologies like HSPA. 5G further increases speeds and dramatically reduces latency compared to 4G.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Summarize services provided by networked hosts
Question: A company deploys a server that stores employee files and allows authenticated users to access them from any network-connected device. What server role does this represent?
A) Web server
B) File server
C) Mail server
D) DNS server
Correct: B
Explanation: A file server stores and manages shared files and directories, allowing authorised network users to access, store, and retrieve documents from a central location. Web servers host and deliver website content using HTTP/HTTPS. Mail servers handle the sending, receiving, and storage of email messages.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Summarize services provided by networked hosts
Question: Which network appliance inspects traffic for malicious activity and can actively block detected threats in real time?
A) IDS
B) Proxy server
C) IPS
D) UTM
Correct: C
Explanation: An IPS (Intrusion Prevention System) sits inline with network traffic, inspects packets for known attack signatures and anomalies, and can actively drop or block malicious traffic in real time. An IDS (Intrusion Detection System) monitors and alerts on suspicious activity but does not block traffic itself. A UTM (Unified Threat Management) device combines multiple security functions including IPS capability in one appliance.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Summarize services provided by networked hosts
Question: A UTM appliance is deployed at a company's network perimeter. Which combination of functions would a UTM typically provide?
A) DHCP, DNS, and file sharing
B) Firewall, IDS/IPS, content filtering, and antivirus
C) Web hosting, email, and database services
D) VoIP, video conferencing, and streaming
Correct: B
Explanation: A UTM (Unified Threat Management) device consolidates multiple security functions into a single appliance, typically including stateful firewall, IDS/IPS, content filtering, antivirus/antimalware scanning, and VPN capabilities. This simplifies security management for small and medium businesses that cannot afford separate specialised appliances for each function. DHCP and DNS are infrastructure services, not security functions associated with UTM.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Summarize services provided by networked hosts
Question: A network proxy server is deployed to control employee internet access. What is a primary function of a proxy server?
A) Assign IP addresses to client workstations
B) Translate hostnames to IP addresses for web browsing
C) Act as an intermediary between clients and external servers to filter and cache content
D) Route packets between different network segments
Correct: C
Explanation: A proxy server acts as an intermediary for client requests, forwarding them to external servers on the client's behalf. This allows the proxy to filter content, cache frequently requested resources to improve performance, log user activity, and hide internal IP addresses. DHCP assigns IP addresses, DNS resolves hostnames, and routers route packets between segments.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Summarize services provided by networked hosts
Question: An industrial facility uses embedded controllers that run a proprietary real-time OS without regular security updates. How should these legacy/embedded systems be treated on the network?
A) Place them on the main corporate network for easy monitoring
B) Disable all network connectivity to prevent any risk
C) Segment them onto isolated VLANs with strict firewall rules
D) Install standard antivirus software to keep them secure
Correct: C
Explanation: Legacy and embedded systems that cannot be patched should be network-segmented onto isolated VLANs with strict ACLs and firewall rules that allow only the minimum required communication. This reduces the attack surface while keeping them operational, since disabling connectivity may render them non-functional in their operational role. Standard antivirus may not be compatible with specialised real-time operating systems used in industrial controllers.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Summarize services provided by networked hosts
Question: A company's DHCP server fails. What is the most immediate symptom users will experience?
A) Web pages will display security certificate errors
B) Network-connected devices will be unable to obtain IP addresses automatically
C) Email delivery will be delayed
D) DNS queries will return incorrect results
Correct: B
Explanation: If the DHCP server is unavailable, client devices that are configured to obtain their IP addresses automatically will fail to receive an address lease and will typically assign themselves an APIPA address (169.254.x.x), losing connectivity to network resources. Devices with statically configured IP addresses will be unaffected. Web certificate errors and DNS issues are separate from DHCP failure.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Summarize services provided by networked hosts
Question: A company's print server receives print jobs from users and manages the queue. What is the benefit of using a dedicated print server over direct printing?
A) Eliminates the need for physical printers
B) Centralises print queue management and reduces direct network connections to printers
C) Encrypts all print jobs with TLS automatically
D) Converts all documents to PDF before printing
Correct: B
Explanation: A print server centralises the management of multiple printers, queuing print jobs and distributing them efficiently without requiring each workstation to maintain a direct connection to every printer. This simplifies administration, enables accounting and auditing of print usage, and allows printers to be shared without leaving them exposed directly on the network. Print servers do not inherently encrypt jobs or convert document formats.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Summarize services provided by networked hosts
Question: IoT devices such as smart thermostats and IP cameras introduce security concerns on enterprise networks. What is the best practice for integrating these devices?
A) Connect them directly to the primary VLAN for maximum bandwidth
B) Use static IP addresses to track each device individually
C) Place them on a separate IoT VLAN with restricted access to core systems
D) Disable WPA2 to ensure maximum device compatibility
Correct: C
Explanation: IoT devices often have weak or unpatched security, making them attractive targets for attackers. Placing them on a dedicated, isolated VLAN with firewall rules that prevent lateral movement to core corporate systems limits the blast radius if a device is compromised. Using static IPs helps with tracking but does not prevent lateral movement. Disabling WPA2 would make the wireless network far less secure.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Install and configure basic wired/wireless SOHO networks
Question: When placing a wireless access point in a SOHO environment, which location provides the best coverage for a single-story office?
A) In a corner of the building for maximum signal reflection
B) Near the floor to minimise interference with desk equipment
C) Centrally located, mounted high on the wall or ceiling
D) Adjacent to the DSL modem to minimise cable length
Correct: C
Explanation: Mounting a wireless AP centrally and at height (ceiling or high on a wall) maximises omnidirectional signal coverage and reduces obstacles that could attenuate the signal. Placing an AP in a corner results in much of the signal radiating outside the building. The AP should be positioned to serve users, not necessarily near the modem — cable length between modem and AP is not a primary concern with structured cabling.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Install and configure basic wired/wireless SOHO networks
Question: A SOHO router needs to allow an internal web server to be accessible from the internet. Which configuration is required?
A) MAC address filtering
B) Port forwarding
C) DNS poisoning
D) SSID broadcast disabling
Correct: B
Explanation: Port forwarding (also called destination NAT or DNAT) directs inbound traffic arriving on a specific external port to the internal IP address and port of the target server. Without port forwarding, inbound connections from the internet cannot reach devices behind NAT. MAC filtering controls which devices can connect to the wireless network and does not affect inbound internet access.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Install and configure basic wired/wireless SOHO networks
Question: A technician is deploying IP phones on a SOHO network using a PoE switch. What must be verified before connecting the phones?
A) That the switch supports the 802.11ac standard
B) That the switch's PoE power budget is sufficient for all connected devices
C) That each phone has a static IP address configured
D) That the router has QoS disabled to prevent prioritisation conflicts
Correct: B
Explanation: Each PoE port can supply a limited wattage (15.4W for 802.3af or 30W for 802.3at), and the switch has an overall power budget shared across all PoE ports. If the total power demand of connected devices exceeds the switch's budget, some devices will not receive power. Static IPs are optional; phones can use DHCP, and QoS should typically be enabled, not disabled, for VoIP traffic.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Install and configure basic wired/wireless SOHO networks
Question: After setting up a SOHO router, a technician wants to ensure the firmware is current. Why is keeping router firmware updated important?
A) Updated firmware increases the router's wireless transmission power
B) Firmware updates improve compatibility with legacy protocols
C) Firmware updates patch security vulnerabilities and fix bugs
D) Updated firmware automatically reconfigures port forwarding rules
Correct: C
Explanation: Router firmware updates frequently include patches for security vulnerabilities, some of which can be exploited remotely to gain control of the device. Manufacturers release firmware updates to address known CVEs and stability issues. Firmware updates do not automatically change security configurations or increase transmission power, and they do not inherently improve legacy protocol compatibility.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Install and configure basic wired/wireless SOHO networks
Question: A parent wants to prevent children from accessing inappropriate websites on a home network without installing software on each device. Which router feature should be configured?
A) MAC address reservation
B) DMZ hosting
C) Content filtering
D) WPS
Correct: C
Explanation: Content filtering configured on the router inspects and blocks DNS requests or HTTP/HTTPS connections to websites in prohibited categories, affecting all devices connected to the network without requiring per-device software installation. MAC address reservation assigns consistent IPs to devices but does not filter content. DMZ hosting exposes a device directly to the internet, which is the opposite of restricting access.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Install and configure basic wired/wireless SOHO networks
Question: A SOHO cable installation requires that patch cables be run neatly along walls and through cable managers. What is the main purpose of proper cable management?
A) Increase the maximum data rate of Cat5e cables
B) Reduce electromagnetic interference by keeping cables grouped tightly
C) Facilitate troubleshooting, airflow, and physical organisation
D) Prevent MAC address conflicts between network devices
Correct: C
Explanation: Proper cable management improves physical organisation, making it easier to trace and troubleshoot connections, and also improves airflow in equipment racks, which is important for cooling. Keeping cables neatly routed reduces the risk of accidental disconnection and damage. Cable management does not change the electrical characteristics of the cables or affect MAC address assignments.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Install and configure basic wired/wireless SOHO networks
Question: A SOHO firewall is being configured to protect the internal network. Which rule is the most fundamental security baseline?
A) Allow all inbound traffic by default; block known malicious IPs
B) Block all inbound traffic by default; allow only specific required services
C) Allow all outbound traffic; block inbound HTTPS only
D) Mirror inbound and outbound rules for symmetry
Correct: B
Explanation: The fundamental principle of firewall security is a default-deny stance for inbound traffic: block everything unless explicitly permitted. This minimises the attack surface by ensuring only intentionally opened ports are accessible. Allowing all inbound traffic by default is extremely dangerous, as it exposes every service running on internal devices to the internet.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Install and configure basic wired/wireless SOHO networks
Question: A technician changes the default administrator password on a new SOHO router immediately after deployment. Why is this step critical?
A) The default password enforces WPA3 encryption automatically
B) Default credentials are publicly known and can be exploited to gain full router control
C) Changing the password enables the router's firewall feature
D) The router will not function without a custom password
Correct: B
Explanation: Router manufacturers ship devices with well-known default credentials (often "admin/admin" or "admin/password") that are documented online and exploited by attackers and botnets. Changing the default password is one of the first and most important hardening steps for any network device. Default passwords do not control encryption or firewall functionality, and the router functions normally with default credentials.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.6 — Compare and contrast common network configuration concepts
Question: A host is configured with IP address 192.168.1.50 and subnet mask 255.255.255.0. What is the network address for this subnet in CIDR notation?
A) 192.168.1.50/24
B) 192.168.1.0/24
C) 192.168.0.0/16
D) 192.168.1.0/25
Correct: B
Explanation: A subnet mask of 255.255.255.0 corresponds to a /24 prefix in CIDR notation, meaning the first 24 bits are the network portion. The network address is formed by setting the host bits to zero: 192.168.1.0. The host address 192.168.1.50 falls within this /24 subnet, which has a range of 192.168.1.1 through 192.168.1.254 for usable hosts.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.6 — Compare and contrast common network configuration concepts
Question: Which technology allows multiple devices on a private LAN to share a single public IP address when accessing the internet?
A) VLAN
B) DHCP
C) NAT/PAT
D) DNS
Correct: C
Explanation: NAT (Network Address Translation) and specifically PAT (Port Address Translation, also called NAT overload) allow many private IP addresses to share a single public IP by mapping each internal session to a unique port number on the public IP. This conserves public IPv4 addresses and also provides a layer of obscurity for internal hosts. VLANs segment networks logically, DHCP assigns IPs, and DNS resolves hostnames.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.6 — Compare and contrast common network configuration concepts
Question: A device is configured with the address 169.254.15.3. What does this address indicate?
A) The device has a valid DHCP lease
B) The device is using a manually configured static IP
C) The device has failed to obtain a DHCP address and is using an APIPA address
D) The device is a DHCP server
Correct: C
Explanation: Addresses in the 169.254.0.0/16 range are APIPA (Automatic Private IP Addressing) addresses, which a Windows device assigns itself when DHCP is unavailable. An APIPA address allows local link communication but does not provide internet access or connectivity to routers. This is a strong diagnostic indicator that the DHCP server is unreachable or the lease has expired.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.6 — Compare and contrast common network configuration concepts
Question: A company wants to logically separate departments on the same physical switch infrastructure without purchasing additional hardware. Which technology enables this?
A) VPN
B) VLAN
C) NAT
D) DHCP
Correct: B
Explanation: VLANs (Virtual Local Area Networks) allow a single physical switch to be logically divided into multiple isolated broadcast domains, effectively separating departments such as HR, Finance, and Engineering without separate physical switches. Traffic between VLANs requires routing, which provides an additional security control point. VPNs provide encrypted tunnels over public networks, not LAN segmentation.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.6 — Compare and contrast common network configuration concepts
Question: What is the primary advantage of IPv6 over IPv4 in terms of addressing?
A) IPv6 uses simpler subnet masks expressed in decimal
B) IPv6 provides a vastly larger address space with 128-bit addresses
C) IPv6 requires NAT to conserve addresses
D) IPv6 is faster than IPv4 because it uses shorter headers
Correct: B
Explanation: IPv6 uses 128-bit addresses, providing approximately 3.4 × 10^38 unique addresses, which is astronomically more than IPv4's approximately 4.3 billion (2^32) addresses. This eliminates the need for NAT, as every device can have a unique globally routable address. IPv6 headers are actually larger than IPv4 headers, but they are more efficient because they eliminated optional fields that caused processing overhead.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.6 — Compare and contrast common network configuration concepts
Question: A remote worker needs secure access to corporate network resources over the internet. Which technology creates an encrypted tunnel to accomplish this?
A) VLAN
B) VPN
C) DHCP reservation
D) Port forwarding
Correct: B
Explanation: A VPN (Virtual Private Network) creates an encrypted tunnel between the remote client and the corporate network, allowing the user to access internal resources as if they were physically on-site. Common VPN protocols include IPSec, SSL/TLS (OpenVPN), and WireGuard. VLANs segment on-premises networks, DHCP reservations assign consistent IPs, and port forwarding exposes services but does not create encrypted client access.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.6 — Compare and contrast common network configuration concepts
Question: A network has been assigned the block 10.10.10.0/26. How many usable host addresses are available in this subnet?
A) 30
B) 62
C) 126
D) 254
Correct: B
Explanation: A /26 subnet mask leaves 6 host bits (32 - 26 = 6), giving 2^6 = 64 total addresses. Subtracting the network address and broadcast address leaves 62 usable host addresses. A /27 gives 30 usable hosts, /25 gives 126, and /24 gives 254 usable hosts.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.6 — Compare and contrast common network configuration concepts
Question: A workstation is unable to reach hosts on other subnets but can communicate with devices on its own subnet. What configuration element is most likely missing or incorrect?
A) Subnet mask
B) DNS server address
C) Default gateway
D) DHCP lease time
Correct: C
Explanation: The default gateway is the router address that a host sends traffic to when the destination is outside its local subnet. Without a correct default gateway, the host has no way to forward traffic to remote networks. The subnet mask determines local vs. remote destinations; DNS resolves names but does not affect routing; and DHCP lease time controls how long an IP assignment is valid.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.6 — Compare and contrast common network configuration concepts
Question: Which IPv6 address type is equivalent to IPv4's APIPA (169.254.x.x) and is automatically configured on every IPv6-enabled interface?
A) Global unicast address
B) Multicast address
C) Link-local address
D) Anycast address
Correct: C
Explanation: IPv6 link-local addresses always start with the prefix FE80::/10 and are automatically configured on every IPv6-enabled interface using EUI-64 or random generation. Like IPv4 APIPA addresses, they are only valid for communication on the local link and are not routable beyond the local segment. Global unicast addresses (analogous to public IPv4 addresses) are needed for internet communication.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.7 — Compare and contrast internet connection types, network types, and their features
Question: Which internet connection type uses existing telephone lines and is typically limited to a few kilometres from the central office due to signal attenuation?
A) Fiber optic
B) Cable (DOCSIS)
C) DSL
D) Satellite
Correct: C
Explanation: DSL (Digital Subscriber Line) transmits data over standard copper telephone lines using frequencies above the voice band, and performance degrades significantly with distance from the ISP's DSLAM (Digital Subscriber Line Access Multiplexer) at the central office. Fiber optic connections use light and are not subject to the same distance limitations. Cable uses coaxial TV infrastructure, and satellite uses geostationary or LEO satellites.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.7 — Compare and contrast internet connection types, network types, and their features
Question: Which network type spans a geographic area such as a city or campus, larger than a LAN but smaller than a WAN?
A) PAN
B) LAN
C) WAN
D) MAN
Correct: D
Explanation: A MAN (Metropolitan Area Network) spans a geographic area such as a city or large campus, larger than a LAN (typically a single building or floor) but smaller than a WAN (wide area network that spans cities, countries, or globally). MANs are often used by municipalities, utilities, or large universities to connect multiple buildings across a city. A PAN is a very short-range personal area network (Bluetooth, NFC).

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.7 — Compare and contrast internet connection types, network types, and their features
Question: A user in a rural area has no access to cable or DSL service. They subscribe to an internet service delivered by a dish antenna pointed at a geostationary satellite. What is a key disadvantage of this connection type?
A) Very low data transfer speeds
B) High latency due to the 35,000 km distance to the satellite
C) Requires a fibre optic cable to the premise
D) Only available in urban areas
Correct: B
Explanation: Geostationary satellites orbit at approximately 35,786 km above the equator, causing round-trip latency of approximately 600 ms or more, which negatively impacts real-time applications like VoIP and online gaming. Download speeds have improved significantly with modern satellite internet, but latency remains the primary limitation. Low Earth Orbit (LEO) satellite services like Starlink significantly reduce this latency to approximately 20-40 ms.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.7 — Compare and contrast internet connection types, network types, and their features
Question: Which connection type uses light pulses through glass or plastic strands to transmit data, offering the highest bandwidth and immunity to electromagnetic interference?
A) DSL
B) Coaxial cable
C) Fiber optic
D) Twisted pair copper
Correct: C
Explanation: Fiber optic cables transmit data using pulses of light rather than electrical signals, providing extremely high bandwidth (tens to hundreds of Gbps), very low latency, and complete immunity to electromagnetic interference (EMI). Unlike copper cables, fiber can span much greater distances without signal degradation. Its main disadvantages are higher installation cost and the delicate nature of glass fibre.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.7 — Compare and contrast internet connection types, network types, and their features
Question: A WISP (Wireless Internet Service Provider) connects a rural customer's home using a directional antenna pointed at a tower. Which of the following best describes this service model?
A) Fiber to the home
B) Fixed broadband wireless access
C) Mobile 5G cellular service
D) Cable DOCSIS service
Correct: B
Explanation: A WISP provides fixed broadband wireless access by using point-to-point or point-to-multipoint wireless links between a transmission tower and customer premises antennas. This is a common solution for areas where running fiber or coaxial cable is economically unfeasible. Unlike cellular service, which supports mobile devices, fixed wireless from a WISP uses stationary directional equipment at the subscriber's location.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.7 — Compare and contrast internet connection types, network types, and their features
Question: A user connects their laptop and smartphone together directly via Bluetooth to transfer a file. What type of network does this represent?
A) LAN
B) WAN
C) MAN
D) PAN
Correct: D
Explanation: A PAN (Personal Area Network) is a very short-range network connecting personal devices in the immediate vicinity of an individual, typically within 10 metres. Bluetooth and USB tethering are common PAN technologies. A LAN covers a building or campus, a MAN covers a city, and a WAN covers large geographic areas.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.7 — Compare and contrast internet connection types, network types, and their features
Question: Which internet connection type delivers data via coaxial cable using the DOCSIS standard and is shared among subscribers in a neighbourhood segment?
A) DSL
B) Fiber (FTTH)
C) Cable broadband
D) ISDN
Correct: C
Explanation: Cable broadband uses the DOCSIS standard over the same coaxial cable infrastructure used for cable TV. Bandwidth is shared among users in the same cable segment, so performance can degrade during peak hours in densely populated areas. DSL uses telephone lines, fiber uses optical cables, and ISDN is a legacy digital telephone circuit technology.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.7 — Compare and contrast internet connection types, network types, and their features
Question: A national retail chain connects all of its stores to a central headquarters using dedicated leased lines and MPLS circuits. What type of network infrastructure does this describe?
A) WLAN
B) LAN
C) PAN
D) WAN
Correct: D
Explanation: A WAN (Wide Area Network) spans large geographic areas — cities, countries, or even globally — connecting multiple geographically dispersed sites such as retail branches to a headquarters. WANs typically use leased lines, MPLS, or internet-based VPNs from carriers. A LAN is confined to a single building or campus, and a WLAN is a wireless LAN.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.8 — Use networking tools
Question: A technician needs to terminate a Cat6 Ethernet cable with an RJ-45 connector. Which tool is required for this task?
A) Punchdown tool
B) Cable stripper
C) Crimper
D) Loopback plug
Correct: C
Explanation: A crimper (RJ-45 crimper) is used to attach an RJ-45 connector to the end of an Ethernet cable by pressing the connector's pins through the cable jacket to make electrical contact with each wire. A cable stripper removes the outer jacket to expose the individual wires before crimping. A punchdown tool is used to terminate cables into patch panels or keystone jacks, not RJ-45 connectors.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.8 — Use networking tools
Question: A technician needs to trace an unlabelled network cable through a wall to identify which patch panel port it terminates at. Which tool should be used?
A) Cable tester
B) Wi-Fi analyser
C) Toner probe (tone generator and probe)
D) Loopback plug
Correct: C
Explanation: A tone generator injects a signal onto the cable at one end, and the probe (inductive amplifier) is used at the patch panel or other suspected termination point to audibly detect the tone, identifying the correct cable without cutting into the wall. A cable tester verifies continuity and wiring order but cannot trace an unlabelled cable through walls. A Wi-Fi analyser is used for wireless networks, not physical cable tracing.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.8 — Use networking tools
Question: A technician wants to verify that a network card is functioning correctly without connecting it to any network device. Which tool should be used?
A) Cable tester
B) Punchdown tool
C) Wi-Fi analyser
D) Loopback plug
Correct: D
Explanation: A loopback plug connects a device's transmit pins directly to its receive pins, allowing the NIC or port to send and receive test data to itself, confirming the hardware is functional independently of any external network. A cable tester checks the continuity and pinout of a network cable, not a NIC. Wi-Fi analysers are for wireless network diagnostics.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.8 — Use networking tools
Question: After installing a wireless network in a multi-tenant office building, a technician needs to identify neighbouring APs, their channels, and signal strengths. Which tool is appropriate?
A) Toner probe
B) Wi-Fi analyser
C) Cable tester
D) Network tap
Correct: B
Explanation: A Wi-Fi analyser (available as a software app or dedicated hardware device) scans the wireless environment and displays all visible access points, their SSIDs, channels, signal strength (RSSI), and security type. This information is essential for identifying channel conflicts and optimising AP placement and channel assignments. A toner probe is for physical cable tracing, and a cable tester checks wired cable integrity.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.8 — Use networking tools
Question: A technician is terminating horizontal cabling into a patch panel in a wiring closet. Which tool is used to seat the wires into the 110-style IDC (Insulation Displacement Connector) blocks?
A) Crimper
B) Cable stripper
C) Punchdown tool
D) Wire snips only
Correct: C
Explanation: A punchdown tool (also called an impact tool) seats individual wire strands into IDC connectors on 110-block patch panels and keystone jacks, cutting the excess wire simultaneously with a blade on the tool. Using wire snips alone does not seat the wire properly into the IDC contacts. A crimper is used for RJ-45 connectors, not IDC-type terminations.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.8 — Use networking tools
Question: A technician suspects a cable run has a wiring fault (reversed pairs or split pairs) after users report intermittent connectivity. Which tool will confirm this?
A) Toner probe
B) Loopback plug
C) Cable tester
D) Multimeter
Correct: C
Explanation: A cable tester sends a signal through each wire pair and displays the pinout mapping, immediately identifying faults such as opens (broken wires), shorts, reversed pairs, split pairs, or crossed connections. A toner probe identifies which cable is which but does not test wiring integrity. A loopback plug tests a port, not the cable run between two termination points.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.8 — Use networking tools
Question: A security engineer needs to capture and analyse all network traffic passing through a specific point on the network without interrupting data flow. Which device should be deployed?
A) Loopback plug
B) Network tap
C) Patch panel
D) Wi-Fi analyser
Correct: B
Explanation: A network tap (Test Access Point) is a passive or active hardware device that creates a copy of all traffic passing through a network link and sends it to a monitoring or analysis device such as a packet analyser, without interrupting the data flow on the live link. Unlike port mirroring on a switch, a hardware tap captures every packet including those that might be missed by software-based mirroring. A loopback plug tests individual ports, not live traffic flows.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.8 — Use networking tools
Question: A technician is creating a custom-length Cat6 patch cable. In the correct sequence of steps, which action immediately precedes using the crimper?
A) Test the cable with a cable tester
B) Strip the outer jacket with a cable stripper, untwist pairs, arrange wires, and insert into the RJ-45 connector
C) Use the punchdown tool to seat wires
D) Inject a tone signal with the tone generator
Correct: B
Explanation: The correct sequence for making a patch cable is: cut the cable to length, strip the outer jacket using a cable stripper, untwist and arrange the wire pairs in the correct T568A or T568B order, trim the wires to equal length, insert them fully into the RJ-45 connector, and then crimp with the crimper. The cable tester is used after crimping to verify the finished cable. A punchdown tool and tone generator are used for different tasks.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast TCP and UDP ports, protocols, and their purposes
Question: A technician is asked to explain why UDP is used for DNS queries instead of TCP. What is the primary reason?
A) UDP provides guaranteed delivery for DNS responses
B) UDP is faster for small transactions because it has no connection establishment overhead
C) TCP does not support the DNS protocol
D) UDP encrypts DNS traffic automatically
Correct: B
Explanation: UDP is connectionless, so it does not require the TCP three-way handshake before sending data, making it significantly faster for small request-response transactions like DNS queries that typically fit within a single packet. The overhead of establishing and tearing down a TCP connection would be disproportionate to the size of most DNS queries. DNS does use TCP as a fallback for large responses and zone transfers, so TCP does support DNS.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast TCP and UDP ports, protocols, and their purposes
Question: A technician is configuring firewall rules and needs to allow outbound POP3 traffic for email retrieval. Which port must be permitted?
A) 25
B) 110
C) 143
D) 587
Correct: B
Explanation: POP3 (Post Office Protocol version 3) uses port 110 for retrieving email from a mail server to the client device. Unlike IMAP, POP3 typically downloads and deletes messages from the server, storing them locally. Port 25 is SMTP (server-to-server), port 143 is IMAP, and port 587 is authenticated SMTP submission.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast common networking hardware
Question: An administrator needs to connect a new building to the existing network without purchasing a new switch. They have available a device that regenerates signals at Layer 1 but provides no filtering or MAC address learning. What device is this?
A) Bridge
B) Router
C) Repeater
D) Hub
Correct: C
Explanation: A repeater operates at OSI Layer 1 (Physical) and simply regenerates (amplifies and retimes) a signal to extend cable length, providing no intelligence such as MAC address learning or traffic filtering. A hub also operates at Layer 1 but has multiple ports; a bridge operates at Layer 2 and can learn MAC addresses and filter traffic between segments. A router operates at Layer 3.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Compare and contrast protocols for wireless networking
Question: A warehouse manager wants to deploy sensors on pallets to track inventory using a low-power mesh network. Which wireless technology is most suitable for battery-powered IoT sensors that need to communicate short distances?
A) 802.11ac
B) Zigbee
C) 4G LTE
D) Bluetooth Classic
Correct: B
Explanation: Zigbee is a low-power mesh networking protocol based on IEEE 802.15.4, designed specifically for IoT applications such as sensor networks, smart home devices, and industrial monitoring. It operates at 2.4 GHz with very low power consumption, enabling battery-powered devices to operate for months or years. 802.11ac consumes far more power, 4G LTE requires cellular service, and Bluetooth Classic is point-to-point rather than mesh.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Summarize services provided by networked hosts
Question: A company's internal website resolves correctly when accessed by name from inside the office but not from home. The DNS server is likely hosted internally. What type of DNS deployment does this describe?
A) Public authoritative DNS
B) Split-horizon (split-brain) DNS
C) DNSSEC-enabled recursive resolver
D) Anycast DNS
Correct: B
Explanation: Split-horizon (split-brain) DNS provides different DNS responses for internal and external queries, giving internal users the private IP address of a server while external users receive the public IP. In this scenario, internal DNS resolves the name correctly but the external DNS records may point elsewhere or may not exist. This is a common configuration for organisations hosting internal web applications.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Install and configure basic wired/wireless SOHO networks
Question: A SOHO router's wireless network is set to WPA2-Personal. A security audit recommends upgrading to the latest standard. Which protocol should replace WPA2-Personal?
A) WEP
B) WPA
C) WPA3-Personal
D) TKIP
Correct: C
Explanation: WPA3-Personal is the current successor to WPA2-Personal, using SAE (Simultaneous Authentication of Equals) instead of the PSK handshake, which eliminates offline dictionary attacks. WEP is severely deprecated and broken. WPA (version 1) and TKIP were interim solutions with known vulnerabilities. WPA3 provides much stronger protection, especially against offline brute-force attacks.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.6 — Compare and contrast common network configuration concepts
Question: A technician configures a DHCP reservation for a network printer so it always receives the same IP address. What does the DHCP server use to identify the printer and assign the reserved address?
A) The printer's IP address
B) The printer's MAC address
C) The printer's hostname
D) The printer's subnet mask
Correct: B
Explanation: DHCP reservations (also called static DHCP or DHCP binding) link a specific IP address to a client's unique MAC (hardware) address. When the printer sends a DHCP Discover, the server recognises its MAC address and always offers the reserved IP. The IP address is the result of the reservation, not the identifier. Hostnames may not be unique or reliably transmitted in all DHCP implementations.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.7 — Compare and contrast internet connection types, network types, and their features
Question: A technician is asked to compare the latency characteristics of geostationary satellite internet versus 5G cellular for gaming applications. Which statement is accurate?
A) Geostationary satellite has lower latency than 5G due to fewer network hops
B) Both have equal latency since they use similar radio frequencies
C) 5G has much lower latency than geostationary satellite, making it more suitable for gaming
D) Geostationary satellite has lower latency than 5G because it operates at higher altitude
Correct: C
Explanation: Geostationary satellites orbit at approximately 35,786 km, causing round-trip latency of 550-700 ms, which is far too high for real-time gaming. 5G cellular networks target sub-10 ms latency (with theoretical minimums around 1 ms) due to the very short distance between the device and the nearest base station. High latency from geostationary satellite causes severe lag in online gaming, VoIP, and interactive applications.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.8 — Use networking tools
Question: A technician cannot determine where a cable jacket ends and the twisted pairs begin because the outer jacket is stuck. What tool is appropriate for removing the outer jacket of a network cable without damaging the inner wire insulation?
A) Wire cutters
B) Crimper
C) Cable stripper
D) Punchdown tool
Correct: C
Explanation: A cable stripper (also called a jacket stripper or wire stripper set for data cables) is specifically designed to cut through the outer jacket at a controlled depth, preventing the inner wire insulation from being nicked or damaged. Using regular wire cutters risks cutting too deep and nicking the wire conductors, which can cause intermittent faults. The crimper is used after stripping to attach the RJ-45 connector.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast TCP and UDP ports, protocols, and their purposes
Question: An employee is configuring a network monitoring application that needs to receive SNMP trap messages. On which port should the application listen?
A) 161
B) 162
C) 389
D) 514
Correct: B
Explanation: SNMP (Simple Network Management Protocol) uses port 161 for polling (manager queries agents) and port 162 for trap messages (agents proactively send alerts to the manager). The application receiving traps must listen on UDP port 162. Port 389 is LDAP and port 514 is Syslog, both different network management-related protocols.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast common networking hardware
Question: A network administrator needs to connect a 100Base-T device to a Gigabit Ethernet switch. The switch auto-negotiates the connection speed. What is the result?
A) The connection fails because speeds cannot be mixed
B) The switch port operates at 100 Mbps to match the slower device
C) The switch forces the device to upgrade to 1 Gbps
D) The device operates at half-duplex only
Correct: B
Explanation: Ethernet auto-negotiation (IEEE 802.3u) allows switch ports to detect the highest common speed and duplex setting supported by both ends and negotiate down to the lower capability. When a 100Base-T device connects, the switch port will negotiate to 100 Mbps full-duplex, which is the best common capability. The device will not be forced to a speed it does not support, and the connection will succeed at 100 Mbps.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Compare and contrast protocols for wireless networking
Question: A hospital wants to track medical equipment using passive tags that require no battery and are activated by a reader's electromagnetic field. Which technology is most appropriate?
A) NFC
B) Active Bluetooth
C) RFID
D) Zigbee
Correct: C
Explanation: RFID (Radio Frequency Identification) uses passive tags (no battery) that are energised by the electromagnetic field from an RFID reader, making them ideal for asset tracking where battery replacement would be impractical. Passive RFID tags can store unique identifiers that are read within a range of a few centimetres to several metres depending on the frequency used. NFC is a form of RFID but is typically limited to very short ranges (under 4 cm) and is used primarily for interactive applications.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Install and configure basic wired/wireless SOHO networks
Question: A home user notices that when they access their router's admin page after setting up a SOHO network, WPS (Wi-Fi Protected Setup) is enabled by default. What is the security risk of WPS?
A) WPS disables WPA2 encryption when enabled
B) The WPS PIN method is vulnerable to brute-force attacks that can reveal the network password
C) WPS broadcasts the Wi-Fi password over the network in plaintext
D) WPS creates a secondary open SSID visible to nearby devices
Correct: B
Explanation: The WPS PIN method has a design flaw where the 8-digit PIN is verified in two halves, reducing the effective keyspace to only 11,000 combinations, making it vulnerable to a brute-force attack (the Pixie Dust attack and related exploits). An attacker who brute-forces the WPS PIN can retrieve the WPA2 passphrase. The recommended remediation is to disable WPS on the router entirely.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.6 — Compare and contrast common network configuration concepts
Question: An administrator uses CIDR notation 192.168.10.0/28 for a subnet. How many usable host addresses does this subnet provide?
A) 6
B) 14
C) 30
D) 62
Correct: B
Explanation: A /28 subnet mask leaves 4 host bits (32 - 28 = 4), giving 2^4 = 16 total addresses. Subtracting the network address and broadcast address leaves 14 usable host IP addresses. A /29 gives 6 usable hosts, /27 gives 30, and /26 gives 62 usable hosts.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.7 — Compare and contrast internet connection types, network types, and their features
Question: An organisation connects all wireless devices in its headquarters building to a centralised wired network via access points. What type of network does this wireless infrastructure represent?
A) PAN
B) MAN
C) WAN
D) WLAN
Correct: D
