Explanation: A WLAN (Wireless Local Area Network) is a LAN that uses 802.11 wireless technology instead of (or in addition to) wired Ethernet to connect devices within a limited geographic area such as an office building. It provides the same local network connectivity as a wired LAN but uses radio waves. A PAN is personal area (Bluetooth), a MAN covers a city, and a WAN spans large geographic areas.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast common networking hardware
Question: A company deploys a managed switch to separate voice and data traffic on the same physical infrastructure. Which feature of the switch is being used?
A) PoE
B) VLAN
C) NAT
D) STP
Correct: B
Explanation: Managed switches support VLANs, allowing voice and data traffic to be logically separated on the same physical switch. Voice traffic is placed on a dedicated voice VLAN (often called a voice VLAN or auxiliary VLAN on Cisco devices), while data traffic uses a separate data VLAN. This separation improves voice quality and security without requiring separate physical switches. PoE powers the IP phones; STP prevents loops.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Summarize services provided by networked hosts
Question: A company deploys a mail server that stores all employee email and allows access via IMAP from corporate devices. What server role is this?
A) Web server
B) Proxy server
C) Mail server
D) DNS server
Correct: C
Explanation: A mail server handles the sending (using SMTP), receiving, and storage of email messages, and provides client access via protocols such as IMAP or POP3. A web server hosts HTTP/HTTPS content, a proxy server acts as an intermediary for client requests, and a DNS server resolves hostnames. The IMAP access described is characteristic of a mail server configuration.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast TCP and UDP ports, protocols, and their purposes
Question: A security scan identifies port 23 open on a network switch. Why should this be considered a vulnerability?
A) Port 23 is used for encrypted management and should always be open
B) Port 23 (Telnet) transmits management credentials in cleartext, making it susceptible to interception
C) Port 23 is used by SMTP and can be exploited for email relay attacks
D) Port 23 is a high-numbered port that bypasses firewall rules
Correct: B
Explanation: Telnet on port 23 sends all data, including authentication credentials (username and password), in cleartext that can be captured by anyone with access to the network path using a packet sniffer. Network devices should be managed exclusively via SSH on port 22, which encrypts all session data. Discovering open Telnet on managed infrastructure is a high-priority finding in a security audit.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Compare and contrast protocols for wireless networking
Question: A conference centre upgrades its wireless network from 802.11ac to 802.11ax. Users in a crowded expo hall with hundreds of simultaneous wireless devices report significantly better performance. What 802.11ax feature is responsible for this improvement?
A) Beamforming exclusive to 802.11ax
B) OFDMA allowing the AP to serve multiple clients simultaneously in each transmission
C) Operation on the 60 GHz band for higher throughput
D) Elimination of the 2.4 GHz band to reduce interference
Correct: B
Explanation: OFDMA (Orthogonal Frequency Division Multiple Access) is a key feature of 802.11ax (Wi-Fi 6) that subdivides a channel into smaller resource units (RUs) and assigns different RUs to different clients in the same transmission, dramatically improving efficiency in high-density environments. 802.11ac uses OFDM which serves only one client per transmission. 802.11ax operates on both 2.4 GHz and 5 GHz, not 60 GHz (which is 802.11ad/WiGig).

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.6 — Compare and contrast common network configuration concepts
Question: A company with a 192.168.50.0/24 network wants to create four equal-sized subnets. What subnet mask should be applied?
A) 255.255.255.192
B) 255.255.255.224
C) 255.255.255.240
D) 255.255.255.128
Correct: A
Explanation: To divide a /24 into 4 equal subnets, you need 2 additional subnet bits (2^2 = 4 subnets), making the mask a /26 or 255.255.255.192. Each /26 subnet contains 64 addresses (62 usable hosts). 255.255.255.128 (/25) creates only 2 subnets, 255.255.255.224 (/27) creates 8 subnets, and 255.255.255.240 (/28) creates 16 subnets.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Install and configure basic wired/wireless SOHO networks
Question: A technician is setting up a SOHO router and notices it was shipped with a well-known default SSID that reveals the router's manufacturer. What is the security risk of leaving the default SSID?
A) The default SSID disables WPA2 encryption
B) The manufacturer's name in the SSID can help attackers identify the router model and exploit known vulnerabilities
C) Default SSIDs broadcast on channels 1 and 6 simultaneously, causing interference
D) Leaving the default SSID prevents devices from connecting at 5 GHz
Correct: B
Explanation: When the SSID reveals the router model or manufacturer, attackers can use that information to look up default credentials and known CVEs for that specific device, streamlining an attack. Changing the SSID to a non-descriptive name is a basic hardening step that reduces information disclosure. The SSID itself does not control encryption settings, channels, or band selection.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.8 — Use networking tools
Question: A technician runs a Wi-Fi analyser in an office and sees that channel 6 shows significant co-channel interference from seven neighbouring APs. The company's APs are also on channel 6. What should the technician do?
A) Increase transmit power on all company APs to overpower the interference
B) Move company APs to channel 3 to split the difference
C) Reassign company APs to channels 1 and 11 to use non-overlapping spectrum
D) Disable 2.4 GHz on all company APs and operate on 5 GHz only if possible
Correct: C
Explanation: In the 2.4 GHz band, channels 1, 6, and 11 are the three non-overlapping channels. Since channel 6 is severely congested, relocating to channels 1 and 11 places the company APs on channels with no spectral overlap to the congested channel 6 environment. Channel 3 would still partially overlap with both channels 1 and 6, creating additional interference rather than eliminating it. Moving to 5 GHz may also be appropriate but was not listed as a standalone option.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast common networking hardware
Question: A technician configures a Layer 3 switch to route traffic between VLANs. What capability does a Layer 3 switch possess that a Layer 2 switch does not?
A) The ability to learn MAC addresses and populate a forwarding table
B) The ability to make routing decisions based on IP addresses
C) Support for port-based VLANs
D) The ability to provide PoE to connected devices
Correct: B
Explanation: A Layer 3 switch combines the hardware-based forwarding speed of a traditional switch with IP routing capabilities, allowing it to route packets between VLANs without requiring a separate external router. Layer 2 switches forward frames using MAC addresses only and cannot route between IP subnets. Both Layer 2 and Layer 3 switches can support VLANs and MAC address learning; Layer 3 is the differentiator for inter-VLAN routing.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Summarize services provided by networked hosts
Question: A company deploys a web server that hosts an e-commerce site. Which port must be open on the firewall to allow customers to access the site securely?
A) 80
B) 25
C) 443
D) 8080
Correct: C
Explanation: HTTPS on port 443 is required for secure (TLS-encrypted) web transactions, which is essential for any e-commerce site handling customer data and payment information. While port 80 is needed for HTTP, redirecting HTTP to HTTPS on port 443 is standard practice. Port 25 is SMTP for mail, and port 8080 is an alternative HTTP port not typically used for production e-commerce.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.6 — Compare and contrast common network configuration concepts
Question: A technician assigns a workstation the IP 10.0.0.1 with subnet mask 255.0.0.0. What class and CIDR prefix does this represent?
A) Class B, /16
B) Class A, /8
C) Class C, /24
D) Class B, /24
Correct: B
Explanation: The 10.0.0.0/8 range is a Class A private address range defined in RFC 1918, where the first octet identifies the network and the remaining three octets are available for hosts. A /8 prefix (255.0.0.0) provides over 16 million host addresses. Class B uses a /16 (255.255.0.0) and the 172.16.0.0-172.31.255.255 private range; Class C uses /24 (255.255.255.0) for the 192.168.0.0/16 private range.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.7 — Compare and contrast internet connection types, network types, and their features
Question: A small business in a rural location uses a 5G cellular connection as its primary internet service. What is one limitation compared to fibre broadband?
A) 5G cannot support multiple simultaneous users
B) 5G data plans often include monthly data caps and are subject to network congestion
C) 5G does not support TCP/IP protocols
D) 5G is limited to 10 Mbps download speed
Correct: B
Explanation: Mobile data plans, including 5G business plans, frequently include monthly data caps or throttling thresholds above which speeds are reduced, and performance can be affected by local cell tower congestion during peak hours. Fibre broadband typically offers unmetered, consistent bandwidth without data caps. 5G supports multiple users and standard TCP/IP, and modern 5G can deliver hundreds of Mbps in good conditions.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast TCP and UDP ports, protocols, and their purposes
Question: A developer is testing an application that connects to an LDAP directory. The test environment uses port 636. What does this tell the developer about the connection?
A) The connection uses STARTTLS on standard LDAP port 389
B) The connection is unencrypted standard LDAP
C) The connection uses LDAPS — LDAP over SSL/TLS from the start
D) The connection uses Kerberos authentication on the LDAP channel
Correct: C
Explanation: Port 636 is the designated port for LDAPS (LDAP Secure), which establishes an SSL/TLS-encrypted connection before any directory data is exchanged. This is distinct from LDAP on port 389 with STARTTLS, which begins unencrypted and then upgrades to TLS. The developer can be assured the directory connection is encrypted from the outset when using port 636.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Compare and contrast protocols for wireless networking
Question: A store deploys a system where customers can tap their smartphone to a point-of-sale terminal to trigger a loyalty programme registration, not a payment. The system needs a very short range to prevent accidental triggers. Which technology is most appropriate?
A) Bluetooth LE
B) NFC
C) Zigbee
D) RFID at 13.56 MHz
Correct: B
Explanation: NFC operates at 13.56 MHz with an intentionally very short range of under 4 cm, making it ideal for deliberate tap-based interactions where accidental triggering must be minimised. While RFID also uses 13.56 MHz, NFC is the interactive, bidirectional standard built into modern smartphones for tap-to-interact use cases. Bluetooth LE has a much longer range (up to 100 metres) making accidental triggers far more likely.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Install and configure basic wired/wireless SOHO networks
Question: A SOHO network user wants to host a game server at home that external friends can connect to. The router uses NAT. What configuration must be made on the router?
A) Enable UPnP and disable the firewall entirely
B) Configure port forwarding to map the game's external port to the internal server IP and port
C) Assign the game server a public IP address from the ISP
D) Create a VLAN for the game server on the router
Correct: B
Explanation: Port forwarding maps an inbound connection arriving on a specific external port to the correct internal (private) IP address and port of the game server behind NAT. Without this, the router has no way to know which internal device should receive unsolicited inbound game traffic. Disabling the firewall entirely would expose all devices, and assigning a public IP is typically not available or necessary in a SOHO setup.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast common networking hardware
Question: A network engineer is designing a resilient network with redundant switch links but wants to prevent loops. Which protocol should be enabled on the switches?
A) VLAN Trunking Protocol (VTP)
B) Spanning Tree Protocol (STP)
C) Link Aggregation Control Protocol (LACP)
D) Dynamic Host Configuration Protocol (DHCP)
Correct: B
Explanation: STP (Spanning Tree Protocol, IEEE 802.1D) and its modern variants (RSTP, MSTP) detect and prevent switching loops by placing redundant ports in a blocking state, ensuring only one active path exists between any two network nodes. Without STP, redundant links would cause broadcast storms and MAC address table instability. VTP manages VLAN information, LACP bundles multiple links, and DHCP assigns IP addresses.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.6 — Compare and contrast common network configuration concepts
Question: A network administrator notices that a device has been assigned the address fe80::1 on its network interface. What type of IPv6 address is this?
A) Global unicast — routable on the internet
B) Multicast — used for one-to-many communication
C) Link-local — valid only on the local network segment
D) Loopback — used for testing the local interface
Correct: C
Explanation: fe80::/10 is the IPv6 link-local prefix, and addresses in this range are automatically configured on every IPv6-enabled interface using EUI-64 or a random algorithm. Link-local addresses are non-routable and only valid for communication within the local network segment (link). The IPv6 loopback address is ::1, while global unicast addresses start with 2000::/3.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Summarize services provided by networked hosts
Question: A company's DHCP server is configured with a scope for the 192.168.1.0/24 network. The scope has an exclusion range of 192.168.1.1 through 192.168.1.20. Why would this exclusion be configured?
A) To reserve addresses for wireless clients only
B) To prevent DHCP from assigning addresses used by statically configured devices such as servers, printers, and the router
C) To block those IP addresses from accessing the internet
D) To implement NAT for the excluded address range
Correct: B
Explanation: DHCP exclusion ranges prevent the server from dynamically assigning IP addresses that are already in use by statically configured infrastructure devices such as the default gateway, servers, printers, and network equipment. Without exclusions, the DHCP server might assign an address already manually configured on another device, causing an IP conflict. Exclusions have no effect on internet access or NAT.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.8 — Use networking tools
Question: A technician uses a multimeter to test a Cat5e cable and measures continuity. The cable passes the continuity test but the network connection is still unreliable. Which dedicated tool would provide a more thorough diagnosis of the cable's wiring order and pair integrity?
A) Wi-Fi analyser
B) Loopback plug
C) Cable tester
D) Toner probe
Correct: C
Explanation: A dedicated cable tester (such as a Fluke MicroScanner or similar) checks not only continuity but also verifies correct pin-to-pin wiring order, identifies split pairs, reversed pairs, shorts, and crossed connections — faults that a simple multimeter continuity test cannot detect. Split pairs, for example, will pass a continuity test but cause significant crosstalk and performance degradation. A cable tester is the correct tool for comprehensive Ethernet cable diagnosis.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast TCP and UDP ports, protocols, and their purposes
Question: A company uses Active Directory for user authentication. Which protocol and port does Active Directory primarily use to allow clients to query the directory for user account information?
A) LDAP on port 389
B) SMTP on port 25
C) SSH on port 22
D) HTTPS on port 443
Correct: A
Explanation: Active Directory is based on LDAP and uses port 389 (or port 636 for LDAPS) for directory queries, including user authentication lookups, group membership queries, and attribute retrieval. Clients and services use LDAP to bind to Active Directory and search for objects. SMTP handles email, SSH handles secure terminal access, and HTTPS handles encrypted web traffic.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Compare and contrast protocols for wireless networking
Question: A technician compares 802.11b and 802.11g. Both operate on the 2.4 GHz band but differ in maximum speed. What are their respective maximum theoretical data rates?
A) 802.11b: 11 Mbps; 802.11g: 54 Mbps
B) 802.11b: 54 Mbps; 802.11g: 11 Mbps
C) 802.11b: 11 Mbps; 802.11g: 300 Mbps
D) 802.11b: 2 Mbps; 802.11g: 11 Mbps
Correct: A
Explanation: 802.11b, released in 1999, operates at 2.4 GHz with a maximum theoretical data rate of 11 Mbps using DSSS (Direct Sequence Spread Spectrum). 802.11g, released in 2003, also operates at 2.4 GHz but uses OFDM to achieve a maximum of 54 Mbps while maintaining backward compatibility with 802.11b. 802.11n increased speeds to 300+ Mbps on 2.4 GHz.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.6 — Compare and contrast common network configuration concepts
Question: A technician needs to configure inter-VLAN routing on a router connected to a managed switch using a single physical interface. Which configuration method achieves this?
A) Configure separate physical interfaces for each VLAN
B) Use a router-on-a-stick configuration with 802.1Q sub-interfaces
C) Configure the router as a DHCP server for all VLANs
D) Enable spanning tree on the router interface
Correct: B
Explanation: Router-on-a-stick uses a single physical router interface connected to a trunk port on the switch, with logical 802.1Q sub-interfaces configured for each VLAN. Each sub-interface has an IP address that serves as the default gateway for its respective VLAN, and the 802.1Q encapsulation tags allow the router to identify and route traffic between VLANs. This approach requires only one physical cable and one switch trunk port.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.7 — Compare and contrast internet connection types, network types, and their features
Question: An ISP advertises an ADSL service with "up to 20 Mbps download and 1 Mbps upload." Why is the upload speed significantly lower than the download speed?
A) ADSL encryption requires more bandwidth for uploads
B) ADSL is asymmetric, allocating more downstream bandwidth to accommodate typical browsing usage patterns
C) Upload traffic is routed through additional ISP infrastructure, adding latency
D) ADSL cannot carry upload and download traffic simultaneously
Correct: B
Explanation: ADSL (Asymmetric Digital Subscriber Line) deliberately allocates much more bandwidth to the downstream direction (ISP to customer) than upstream (customer to ISP), reflecting typical usage where users consume more content than they produce. The word "Asymmetric" in the name describes this characteristic. SDSL (Symmetric DSL) provides equal upload and download speeds but is less common for residential customers.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Summarize services provided by networked hosts
Question: A help desk receives reports that the company's internal website is unreachable by hostname but accessible by IP address. Which server role is most likely malfunctioning?
A) DHCP server
B) DNS server
C) Mail server
D) Proxy server
Correct: B
Explanation: If the site is reachable by IP but not by hostname, the DNS server is not resolving the hostname to the correct IP address — either the DNS server is down, misconfigured, or the DNS record for the internal site is missing or incorrect. DHCP failure would prevent IP assignment, not name resolution. Mail and proxy server failures would not affect web hostname resolution.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast common networking hardware
Question: An enterprise data centre uses a spine-leaf architecture with high-density switches. Each access layer switch connects to both spine switches. Which feature prevents the redundant uplinks from causing broadcast storms?
A) DHCP snooping
B) 802.1Q VLAN tagging
C) Spanning Tree Protocol (STP) or equivalent loop prevention
D) Port mirroring
Correct: C
Explanation: Spanning Tree Protocol (STP) or modern equivalents like RSTP and ECMP (in Layer 3 designs) prevent loops in redundant switch topologies by logically blocking redundant paths while keeping them available for failover. Without loop prevention, redundant physical paths create broadcast storms that can consume all network bandwidth. DHCP snooping is a security feature, 802.1Q tags VLANs, and port mirroring copies traffic for analysis.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Install and configure basic wired/wireless SOHO networks
Question: During a SOHO network installation, a technician needs to connect a wall outlet jack to a patch panel port. Which tool and procedure are used for this structured cabling task?
A) Use a crimper to attach an RJ-45 connector to the horizontal run cable
B) Use a punchdown tool to terminate the cable pairs into IDC connectors on the patch panel
C) Use a cable tester to terminate the cable at both ends
D) Use a tone generator to seat wires into the keystone jack
Correct: B
Explanation: Horizontal cabling runs are terminated into patch panels and keystone jacks using a punchdown tool, which forces each wire conductor into the IDC (Insulation Displacement Connector) contact and simultaneously trims the excess wire. The punchdown tool ensures a reliable gas-tight connection in the IDC slot. RJ-45 crimpers are for patch cable ends, not permanent structured cabling terminations.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.6 — Compare and contrast common network configuration concepts
Question: A small business has one public IP address from its ISP. All internal hosts use private RFC 1918 addresses. When a host sends traffic to the internet, the router translates the private source IP to the public IP. What is this process called?
A) VLAN tagging
B) DNS resolution
C) Network Address Translation (NAT)
D) Dynamic Host Configuration
Correct: C
Explanation: NAT (specifically PAT/NAT overload) translates private source IP addresses to the router's single public IP address, enabling all internal hosts to share internet access. The router maintains a translation table mapping each internal session to a unique source port on the public IP so return traffic can be correctly forwarded to the originating internal host. This is the fundamental mechanism enabling private address use in SOHO and enterprise networks.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast TCP and UDP ports, protocols, and their purposes
Question: A network engineer is asked to explain the difference between TCP and UDP for the A+ exam. Which statement correctly describes TCP compared to UDP?
A) TCP is connectionless and delivers data faster with no error checking
B) TCP is connection-oriented and provides guaranteed delivery with sequencing and error correction
C) TCP uses less overhead than UDP because it sends raw packets without headers
D) TCP is used exclusively for real-time applications like VoIP and streaming
Correct: B
Explanation: TCP (Transmission Control Protocol) is a connection-oriented protocol that establishes a session via a three-way handshake and provides guaranteed, ordered delivery using sequence numbers, acknowledgements, and retransmission of lost segments. UDP (User Datagram Protocol) is connectionless, offers no delivery guarantees, and is preferred for real-time applications where low latency is more important than reliability, such as VoIP and video streaming. TCP's reliability mechanisms add overhead compared to UDP.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.8 — Use networking tools
Question: A technician needs to verify that a newly installed Cat6 cable run from a patch panel to a wall jack passes signal correctly on all eight conductors in the proper wiring order. What is the correct tool and its expected output for a properly wired cable?
A) Toner probe — emits an audible tone at both ends when the cable is intact
B) Cable tester — displays pins 1-8 mapping correctly between both ends (straight-through for T568B)
C) Loopback plug — shows the port as active when inserted into the wall jack
D) Wi-Fi analyser — detects the cable as a network segment
Correct: B
Explanation: A cable tester applies a test signal to each of the eight conductors sequentially and displays the pin mapping between the two ends, confirming that all eight wires are connected, in the correct order (T568A or T568B), with no opens, shorts, or crossed pairs. A toner probe identifies which cable is which but cannot verify pin mapping. A loopback plug tests a switch or NIC port, not a cable run. Wi-Fi analysers are for wireless, not wired cables.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Compare and contrast protocols for wireless networking
Question: A company deploys 5G as a backup WAN link. Which characteristic makes 5G suitable as a resilient failover connection compared to 4G?
A) 5G operates exclusively on licensed spectrum, eliminating interference
B) 5G offers significantly higher throughput and lower latency than 4G, making failover nearly seamless for most applications
C) 5G uses fibre optic backhaul that cannot be disrupted by weather
D) 5G is available without a data plan on public infrastructure
Correct: B
Explanation: 5G's significantly higher throughput (potentially multi-Gbps) and ultra-low latency (sub-10 ms) make it a much more capable failover WAN link than 4G, supporting enterprise workloads such as video conferencing, cloud applications, and VoIP during primary circuit outages. 5G does use licensed spectrum but still shares it among subscribers. 5G RAN (Radio Access Network) uses wireless, not fibre, for the last mile.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Summarize services provided by networked hosts
Question: A company's IDS generates an alert that suspicious port scanning activity was detected originating from an internal workstation. What action does an IDS take upon detection?
A) Automatically blocks the offending workstation at the switch port level
B) Generates an alert and logs the event but does not block the traffic
C) Quarantines the workstation on a separate VLAN automatically
D) Sends a TCP reset to terminate all active connections from the workstation
Correct: B
Explanation: An IDS (Intrusion Detection System) operates in monitoring mode and generates alerts and logs when suspicious activity is detected, but it does not actively block or modify traffic. An IPS (Intrusion Prevention System) sits inline and can actively drop, block, or redirect malicious traffic. Automatic VLAN quarantine and TCP reset injection are active response mechanisms associated with IPS or NAC (Network Access Control) systems, not a passive IDS.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.6 — Compare and contrast common network configuration concepts
Question: A technician is asked what the broadcast address is for the subnet 192.168.5.0/27. What is the correct answer?
A) 192.168.5.31
B) 192.168.5.255
C) 192.168.5.32
D) 192.168.5.30
Correct: A
Explanation: A /27 subnet has 5 host bits (2^5 = 32 addresses per subnet). Starting at 192.168.5.0, the subnet spans 192.168.5.0 through 192.168.5.31. The broadcast address is the last address in the range: 192.168.5.31. 192.168.5.255 is the broadcast for the /24 supernet, 192.168.5.32 is the start of the next /27 subnet, and 192.168.5.30 is the last usable host address.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast common networking hardware
Question: A company implements SD-WAN to manage connectivity across multiple branch offices. Which benefit does SD-WAN provide over traditional WAN configurations?
A) SD-WAN eliminates the need for routers entirely
B) SD-WAN allows centralised policy management and can dynamically route traffic across multiple WAN links based on application requirements
C) SD-WAN requires all WAN links to use the same ISP for consistency
D) SD-WAN provides automatic IP address assignment across WAN links
Correct: B
Explanation: SD-WAN (Software-Defined Wide Area Network) extends SDN concepts to WAN connectivity, enabling centralised management of multiple WAN links (MPLS, broadband, LTE) with dynamic path selection based on application-level policies, link quality metrics, and cost. This improves resilience, performance, and cost efficiency compared to traditional static WAN routing. SD-WAN uses routers and gateways rather than eliminating them, and can use multiple ISPs simultaneously.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.7 — Compare and contrast internet connection types, network types, and their features
Question: An organisation needs to connect two office campuses in different cities over a private, dedicated network path. Which WAN technology provides guaranteed bandwidth and is not shared with other customers?
A) Public internet VPN
B) Cable broadband
C) Dedicated leased line (e.g., T1, E1, or dark fibre)
D) 4G LTE cellular
Correct: C
Explanation: Dedicated leased lines (such as T1, E1, DS3, or dark fibre) provide a private, guaranteed-bandwidth circuit between two locations that is not shared with other customers, ensuring consistent latency and throughput. Public internet VPNs share internet infrastructure and are subject to variable congestion. Cable broadband is a shared medium within a neighbourhood segment. Cellular is shared wireless spectrum.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.5 — Install and configure basic wired/wireless SOHO networks
Question: A technician is configuring a SOHO router to segment a guest wireless network from the main corporate network. Which feature should be enabled to prevent guest users from accessing internal resources?
A) MAC address filtering on the guest SSID
B) Guest network VLAN isolation / guest network mode
C) WPS on the guest SSID
D) DNS filtering on the main SSID
Correct: B
Explanation: Most SOHO routers with a guest network feature place guest SSID traffic on a separate VLAN that is isolated from the main LAN, allowing guests to access the internet while being blocked from seeing internal hosts, printers, and NAS devices. MAC filtering only controls which devices can connect, not what they can access after connecting. WPS is a connection convenience feature and DNS filtering affects web content, not network segmentation.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast TCP and UDP ports, protocols, and their purposes
Question: A network administrator sees traffic destined for port 3389 being blocked by the perimeter firewall on inbound rules. A remote worker reports they cannot access their office desktop remotely. Which protocol requires port 3389 to be permitted?
A) SSH
B) VNC
C) RDP
D) Telnet
Correct: C
Explanation: RDP (Remote Desktop Protocol) uses TCP port 3389 for graphical remote desktop access to Windows systems. The firewall blocking inbound port 3389 prevents external RDP connections. The recommended approach is not to expose RDP directly to the internet (due to brute-force and exploit risk) but instead to use a VPN first and connect via RDP over the VPN tunnel. SSH uses port 22, VNC uses port 5900, and Telnet uses port 23.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.6 — Compare and contrast common network configuration concepts
Question: A workstation receives its IP configuration from DHCP with a lease time of 8 hours. After 4 hours (50% of the lease), what does the DHCP client attempt to do?
A) Release the IP address and request a new one
B) Renew the lease by contacting the DHCP server directly with a unicast request
C) Switch to an APIPA address as a backup
D) Broadcast a new DHCP Discover to find an alternate server
Correct: B
Explanation: At 50% of the lease time (T1), the DHCP client attempts to renew its lease by sending a unicast DHCPREQUEST directly to the original DHCP server. If the server responds with a DHCPACK, the lease is renewed. If renewal fails at T1, the client tries a broadcast renewal at T2 (87.5% of lease time). The client only falls back to APIPA if the lease fully expires without successful renewal and no DHCP server is found.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.8 — Use networking tools
Question: A technician is monitoring network traffic on a switch and needs to capture packets sent between a specific workstation and a server for analysis. The switch does not have a built-in packet capture feature. Which approach should the technician use?
A) Install a Wi-Fi analyser on the workstation
B) Use port mirroring (SPAN) on the switch to copy traffic to a monitoring port connected to a packet analyser
C) Connect a loopback plug to the server's NIC
D) Use a cable tester on the link between the workstation and switch
Correct: B
Explanation: Port mirroring (SPAN — Switched Port Analyser) configures the switch to copy all traffic from one or more source ports to a designated mirror (destination) port, where a device running a packet analyser (such as Wireshark) captures the traffic for analysis. A network hardware tap is an alternative that provides a similar function without relying on switch software. A loopback plug tests port functionality, and cable testers test physical cable integrity.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Compare and contrast protocols for wireless networking
Question: A warehouse deploys a wireless network for barcode scanners that frequently roam between access points throughout the facility. Which feature ensures seamless handoff between APs without dropping the connection?
A) SSID hiding
B) MAC address filtering
C) Fast BSS Transition (802.11r) / seamless roaming
D) WPS push-button pairing
Correct: C
Explanation: 802.11r (Fast BSS Transition) enables fast secure roaming by pre-establishing the security keys with the target AP before the client fully transitions, dramatically reducing the handoff time compared to full re-authentication. This is critical for real-time applications and constantly roaming devices like warehouse scanners where even brief connection interruptions cause data loss. SSID hiding and MAC filtering are security configurations that do not affect roaming behaviour.

Domain: 2.0 Networking
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast common networking hardware
Question: A network administrator is reviewing the benefits of using a managed switch over an unmanaged switch. Which capability is exclusive to a managed switch?
A) Connecting multiple devices via Ethernet ports
B) Forwarding frames based on MAC addresses
C) Configuration of VLANs, port security, and SNMP monitoring
D) Providing PoE power to connected devices
Correct: C
Explanation: Managed switches provide a full management interface (CLI, web GUI, or API) that allows administrators to configure VLANs, port security, QoS, SNMP monitoring, port mirroring, STP settings, and link aggregation. Unmanaged switches forward frames using MAC addresses and support PoE (if PoE-capable) but offer no configuration interface. The ability to segment, monitor, and control network behaviour is the primary value of managed switches in enterprise environments.
Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: Which Ethernet cable category supports speeds up to 10 Gbps at distances up to 55 meters?
A) Cat 5e
B) Cat 6
C) Cat 6a
D) Cat 7
Correct: B
Explanation: Cat 6 cable supports 10 Gbps at distances up to 55 meters using its tighter twist specifications. Cat 5e is limited to 1 Gbps, while Cat 6a extends 10 Gbps to 100 meters. Cat 7 uses shielded pairs and proprietary connectors not part of standard TIA cabling.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: A technician needs to run cable through an air-handling space above a drop ceiling. Which cable jacket type is required?
A) PVC
B) Plenum
C) Riser
D) Direct burial
Correct: B
Explanation: Plenum-rated cable uses a special low-smoke, flame-retardant jacket approved for air-handling spaces such as above drop ceilings. PVC jacket produces toxic fumes when burned and is not permitted in plenum spaces. Riser-rated cable is approved for vertical runs between floors but not for air-handling spaces.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: Which coaxial cable type is most commonly used for cable television (CATV) distribution to homes?
A) RG-59
B) RG-6
C) RG-8
D) RG-58
Correct: B
Explanation: RG-6 coaxial cable is the standard for cable television and satellite distribution because it supports higher frequencies with lower signal loss than RG-59. RG-59 has a thinner center conductor and higher attenuation, making it unsuitable for modern CATV. RG-8 and RG-58 are used in radio frequency and older networking applications.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: A technician is connecting a workstation to a switch in a data center requiring maximum bandwidth over a 1-kilometer run without signal repeaters. Which cable type should be used?
A) Cat 6a
B) Single-mode fiber
C) Multi-mode fiber
D) Cat 8
Correct: B
Explanation: Single-mode fiber uses a narrow 9-micron core and a laser light source, supporting distances of tens of kilometers with minimal signal loss. Multi-mode fiber is limited to approximately 550 meters at 10 Gbps. Copper cable standards like Cat 6a and Cat 8 are limited to 100 meters and 30 meters respectively.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: What is the maximum data transfer rate of USB 3.1 Gen 2?
A) 480 Mbps
B) 5 Gbps
C) 10 Gbps
D) 20 Gbps
Correct: C
Explanation: USB 3.1 Gen 2 (also marketed as USB 3.2 Gen 2) transfers data at 10 Gbps using SuperSpeed+ technology. USB 3.0 and USB 3.1 Gen 1 operate at 5 Gbps, while USB 2.0 is limited to 480 Mbps. USB 4.0 achieves speeds of 20 Gbps or higher.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: Which USB connector type is reversible and used on both hosts and devices in USB 3.1 and later standards?
A) USB-A
B) USB-B
C) USB Micro-B
D) USB-C
Correct: D
Explanation: USB-C features a symmetrical oval connector that can be inserted in either orientation, eliminating the need to orient the plug correctly. USB-A is the rectangular host connector found on computers and is not reversible. USB-B and Micro-B are device-side connectors with specific orientations required for insertion.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: Thunderbolt 3 uses which physical connector type?
A) USB-A
B) DisplayPort
C) USB-C
D) Mini DisplayPort
Correct: C
Explanation: Thunderbolt 3 uses the USB-C physical connector, allowing it to share ports and cables with USB-C devices. It provides 40 Gbps bandwidth and can carry USB, DisplayPort, and PCIe signals simultaneously. Thunderbolt 1 and 2 used the Mini DisplayPort connector form factor.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: Which video connector carries both audio and video signals and is the most common display interface on modern consumer televisions?
A) VGA
B) DVI
C) HDMI
D) DisplayPort
Correct: C
Explanation: HDMI (High-Definition Multimedia Interface) carries both digital audio and digital video over a single cable, making it the standard interface for consumer televisions and home theater equipment. VGA is an analog-only video signal. DVI can carry audio only in some proprietary implementations and is primarily a video-only standard.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: A technician needs to connect an older monitor using a 15-pin D-sub connector. Which interface is being used?
A) DVI-D
B) VGA
C) HDMI
D) DisplayPort
Correct: B
Explanation: VGA (Video Graphics Array) uses a 15-pin DE-15 D-sub connector and transmits an analog video signal. DVI connectors have a different pin layout with a flat pin and a grid of round pins. HDMI and DisplayPort use entirely different connector form factors with no pin-and-socket arrangement.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: Which DVI variant supports only digital signals and is identified by a connector with only round pins and no flat blade?
A) DVI-A
B) DVI-I
C) DVI-D
D) DVI-P
Correct: C
Explanation: DVI-D carries only digital video signals and has a connector consisting of round pins arranged in a grid without the flat four-pin cluster used for analog. DVI-I (Integrated) supports both analog and digital signals and includes the flat blade plus surrounding pins. DVI-A carries only analog signals and is rarely used.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: What is the maximum theoretical bandwidth of Thunderbolt 4?
A) 20 Gbps
B) 40 Gbps
C) 80 Gbps
D) 10 Gbps
Correct: B
Explanation: Thunderbolt 4 operates at a maximum bandwidth of 40 Gbps, the same as Thunderbolt 3 but with stricter minimum requirements for video output and PCIe tunneling. Thunderbolt 5 doubles this to 80 Gbps. Thunderbolt 4 also mandates support for two 4K displays or one 8K display.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: Which cable type uses an LC or SC connector and a 62.5-micron or 50-micron core to carry light signals over shorter distances?
A) Single-mode fiber
B) Multi-mode fiber
C) Coaxial RG-6
D) Cat 8
Correct: B
Explanation: Multi-mode fiber uses a larger core (50 or 62.5 microns) that allows multiple light modes to propagate simultaneously, suitable for distances up to about 550 meters at 10 Gbps. Single-mode fiber uses a 9-micron core and a single light path for much longer distances. RG-6 and Cat 8 are copper-based cables that do not use optical connectors.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: A user's iPhone needs to be connected to a laptop that only has standard USB-A ports. Which cable is needed?
A) USB-C to USB-A
B) Lightning to USB-A
C) Micro-USB to USB-A
D) Mini-USB to USB-A
Correct: B
Explanation: Apple iPhones (pre-USB-C models) use the proprietary Lightning connector, so a Lightning-to-USB-A cable is required to connect to a standard USB-A port. USB-C and Micro-USB are used on Android and other devices. Mini-USB is an older connector no longer used on smartphones.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: Which cable standard supports data rates up to 40 Gbps using Cat 8 copper and is designed for data center top-of-rack switch connections?
A) Cat 6a
B) Cat 7
C) Cat 8
D) Cat 5e
Correct: C
Explanation: Cat 8 cable supports 25 Gbps and 40 Gbps Ethernet at distances up to 30 meters, specifically designed for short data center runs. Cat 7 uses shielded twisted pairs but is not part of the TIA standard and tops out at 10 Gbps in most implementations. Cat 6a reaches 10 Gbps at up to 100 meters but cannot match Cat 8 speeds.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: Which interface standard uses a 7-pin connector for internal storage devices and replaced the older parallel ATA standard?
A) eSATA
B) SCSI
C) SATA
D) IDE
Correct: C
Explanation: SATA (Serial ATA) uses a 7-pin data connector and a 15-pin power connector, replacing the 40-pin ribbon cables of parallel ATA/IDE. eSATA is the external version of SATA using a shielded connector. SCSI uses wide 68-pin or narrow 50-pin connectors for enterprise storage.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: A technician is working on a legacy server with a 68-pin wide connector used for hard drives and tape drives. Which interface is this?
A) IDE
B) SATA
C) SCSI
D) eSATA
Correct: C
Explanation: Wide SCSI (Small Computer System Interface) uses a 68-pin connector and supports multiple devices on a single bus, commonly found in servers and workstations. IDE/PATA uses a 40-pin ribbon connector. SATA uses a narrow 7-pin connector, and eSATA is a shielded external variant of SATA.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: What is the maximum data transfer rate of USB 2.0?
A) 12 Mbps
B) 480 Mbps
C) 5 Gbps
D) 1.5 Mbps
Correct: B
Explanation: USB 2.0 Hi-Speed operates at 480 Mbps, a significant improvement over USB 1.1's 12 Mbps Full Speed mode. USB 3.0 and later standards far exceed this with SuperSpeed rates of 5 Gbps and above. USB 1.0 Low Speed operated at only 1.5 Mbps.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: A technician is setting up a serial console connection to a managed switch using a 9-pin D-sub connector. Which interface is being used?
A) VGA
B) RS-232
C) SCSI
D) eSATA
Correct: B
Explanation: RS-232 serial connections use a DB-9 (DE-9) 9-pin D-sub connector and are commonly used for console management of network equipment. VGA also uses a D-sub connector but has 15 pins and carries video signals. SCSI and eSATA use entirely different connector types for storage connectivity.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Given a scenario, install the appropriate RAM
Question: A workstation motherboard has four memory slots and is populated with two DDR4 sticks in slots 1 and 3. What memory configuration is active?
A) Single channel
B) Dual channel
C) Quad channel
D) ECC mode
Correct: B
Explanation: Populating two matching DIMMs in slots 1 and 3 (or 2 and 4) on a four-slot motherboard activates dual-channel mode, doubling the memory bus width from 64 to 128 bits. Single channel uses only one DIMM or DIMMs not in matching pairs. Quad channel requires four matching DIMMs and is supported only on HEDT and server platforms.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Given a scenario, install the appropriate RAM
Question: Which RAM type is used in laptops and features a smaller form factor with 260 pins for DDR4?
A) DIMM
B) SO-DIMM
C) RIMM
D) ECC DIMM
Correct: B
Explanation: SO-DIMM (Small Outline DIMM) is the compact RAM module used in laptops, small form factor desktops, and some printers, with 260 pins for DDR4. Full-size DIMMs have 288 pins for DDR4 and are used in desktop and server motherboards. RIMMs were the proprietary Rambus memory modules used in late 1990s systems.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Given a scenario, install the appropriate RAM
Question: A server administrator needs RAM that can detect and correct single-bit memory errors to ensure data integrity. Which RAM type is required?
A) DDR4 non-ECC
B) DDR3 SO-DIMM
C) ECC RAM
D) DDR5 XMP
Correct: C
Explanation: ECC (Error Correcting Code) RAM uses additional chips to detect and correct single-bit errors and detect (but not correct) double-bit errors, essential for servers and workstations requiring high data integrity. Non-ECC RAM has no error correction capability. XMP is an Intel overclocking profile for desktop DDR memory.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Given a scenario, install the appropriate RAM
Question: Which DDR generation introduced a maximum speed of 3200 MT/s as its top standard speed and operates at 1.2V?
A) DDR3
B) DDR4
C) DDR5
D) DDR2
Correct: B
Explanation: DDR4 operates at 1.2V (compared to DDR3's 1.5V) and standard speeds range from DDR4-1600 up to DDR4-3200 MT/s. DDR3 tops out at around DDR3-2133 MT/s at 1.5V. DDR5 begins at 4800 MT/s and operates at 1.1V with on-die ECC.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Given a scenario, install the appropriate RAM
Question: A technician is upgrading RAM in a gaming desktop. The motherboard supports DDR5. The user wants to maximize bandwidth. What configuration should the technician recommend?
A) One DDR5 stick of 32 GB
B) Two DDR5 sticks of 16 GB each in dual-channel slots
C) Four DDR4 sticks in quad-channel configuration
D) Two DDR4 sticks in dual-channel slots
Correct: B
Explanation: Two matching DDR5 sticks installed in the correct dual-channel slots doubles the effective memory bandwidth compared to a single stick. DDR4 modules cannot be installed in a DDR5 motherboard as the keying notch positions are different. Quad-channel requires a platform specifically supporting it such as Intel HEDT or AMD Threadripper.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Given a scenario, install the appropriate RAM
Question: What does the CAS latency value in a RAM specification such as CL16 represent?
A) The number of memory channels supported
B) The clock cycles between a read command and data output
C) The operating voltage of the module
D) The number of ranks on the module
Correct: B
Explanation: CAS (Column Address Strobe) latency is the number of clock cycles that elapse between a memory controller issuing a read command and the data becoming available. Lower CAS latency values indicate faster response times. Voltage and rank count are separate specifications listed alongside CAS latency.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Given a scenario, install the appropriate RAM
Question: A technician installs two 8 GB DDR4 sticks alongside two existing 4 GB DDR4 sticks for a total of 24 GB. The system boots but reports instability. What is the most likely cause?
A) The motherboard does not support more than 16 GB
B) Mixing different capacity modules disabled dual-channel operation
C) DDR4 modules cannot be mixed with other DDR4 modules
D) The PSU wattage is insufficient for additional RAM
Correct: B
Explanation: Mixing different-capacity RAM modules can prevent the system from running in dual-channel mode and may cause instability due to differing timings and speeds between the modules. While technically functional in some cases, mixed-capacity kits often require the system to run in single-channel or flex mode. For best stability and performance, matched pairs of identical modules should be used.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Given a scenario, install the appropriate RAM
Question: DDR5 RAM introduces which major architectural change compared to DDR4?
A) Higher operating voltage of 1.5V
B) On-die ECC and on-module power management IC
C) Support for the 240-pin DIMM slot standard
D) Single-channel only operation
Correct: B
Explanation: DDR5 moves the power management circuitry onto the module itself (PMIC) and incorporates on-die ECC for improved data integrity, both significant changes from DDR4. DDR5 actually operates at a lower voltage of 1.1V compared to DDR4's 1.2V. DDR5 DIMMs use 288 pins but with a different notch position than DDR4.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Given a scenario, install the appropriate RAM
Question: Which RAM form factor would a technician install into a standard full-tower desktop motherboard?
A) SO-DIMM
B) MicroDIMM
C) DIMM
D) RIMM
Correct: C
Explanation: Standard desktop motherboards use full-size DIMMs (Dual Inline Memory Modules), which have 288 pins for DDR4 or DDR5. SO-DIMMs are the compact variant for laptops and SFF systems with 260 pins for DDR4. RIMMs were proprietary Rambus modules discontinued over two decades ago.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Given a scenario, install the appropriate RAM
Question: A workstation RAM module is labeled DDR4-3200. What does 3200 refer to?
A) Module capacity in megabytes
B) Data transfer rate in megatransfers per second
C) Module latency in nanoseconds
D) Clock frequency in MHz
Correct: B
Explanation: The number in DDR4-3200 refers to the effective data transfer rate of 3200 megatransfers per second (MT/s), which is double the actual clock speed of 1600 MHz due to DDR's double data rate operation. The "DDR" prefix itself indicates data is transferred on both the rising and falling edges of the clock. Module capacity is expressed in gigabytes separately.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Given a scenario, select and install storage devices
Question: A user wants the fastest possible storage for their new workstation build. Which interface and form factor combination provides the highest sequential read performance?
A) SATA SSD in 2.5-inch form factor
B) mSATA SSD
C) NVMe SSD in M.2 form factor
D) 7200 RPM SATA HDD
Correct: C
Explanation: NVMe (Non-Volatile Memory Express) SSDs using the M.2 form factor connect directly to PCIe lanes, achieving sequential read speeds of 3,500 MB/s or higher on PCIe Gen 3 and over 7,000 MB/s on PCIe Gen 4. SATA SSDs are limited to approximately 550 MB/s due to the SATA III interface. Traditional HDDs top out around 200 MB/s sequentially.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Given a scenario, select and install storage devices
Question: A laptop hard drive uses a 2.5-inch form factor spinning at 5400 RPM. A technician wants to upgrade for better performance without changing form factor. What is the best upgrade?
A) Replace with a 3.5-inch 7200 RPM HDD
B) Replace with a 2.5-inch SATA SSD
C) Add an mSATA SSD as a second drive
D) Replace with a 3.5-inch NVMe SSD
Correct: B
Explanation: A 2.5-inch SATA SSD fits the same drive bay as the existing HDD and uses the same SATA connector, making it a direct drop-in replacement with dramatically improved performance. A 3.5-inch HDD does not fit in a laptop bay. NVMe SSDs in 3.5-inch form do not exist; NVMe uses M.2 or PCIe add-in card form factors.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Given a scenario, select and install storage devices
Question: Which RAID level stripes data across multiple drives for maximum performance with no redundancy, requiring at least two drives?
A) RAID 1
B) RAID 5
C) RAID 0
D) RAID 10
Correct: C
Explanation: RAID 0 stripes data across all member drives, multiplying sequential throughput by the number of drives, but offers no redundancy — a single drive failure loses all data. RAID 1 mirrors data across two drives for redundancy without a performance gain. RAID 5 stripes with distributed parity, balancing performance and fault tolerance.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Given a scenario, select and install storage devices
Question: A small business needs storage that can survive a single drive failure while using space on three drives efficiently. Which RAID level is most appropriate?
A) RAID 0
B) RAID 1
C) RAID 5
D) RAID 10
Correct: C
Explanation: RAID 5 uses distributed parity across all three drives, allowing the array to survive a single drive failure while providing a usable capacity of n-1 drives (two-thirds of total raw capacity in a three-drive set). RAID 1 requires two drives but mirrors only one drive's worth of data. RAID 10 requires at least four drives and combines mirroring and striping.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Given a scenario, select and install storage devices
Question: Which RAID level requires a minimum of four drives and combines the performance of striping with the fault tolerance of mirroring?
A) RAID 0
B) RAID 5
C) RAID 6
D) RAID 10
Correct: D
Explanation: RAID 10 (also called RAID 1+0) mirrors pairs of drives and then stripes across the mirrors, requiring a minimum of four drives, offering both high performance and the ability to survive multiple drive failures as long as no mirror pair loses both drives. RAID 5 requires only three drives but uses parity rather than mirroring. RAID 6 uses dual parity and can survive two simultaneous drive failures.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Given a scenario, select and install storage devices
Question: An enterprise server uses 15,000 RPM hard drives. What is the primary benefit of this rotation speed compared to 7200 RPM drives?
A) Lower power consumption
B) Reduced seek time and higher IOPS
C) Larger storage capacity
D) Compatibility with SATA III interface
Correct: B
Explanation: 15,000 RPM drives have significantly faster rotational speed, reducing rotational latency and improving random I/O operations per second (IOPS), critical for database workloads. Higher RPM drives consume more power and generate more heat than slower drives. Enterprise 15K drives typically use SAS rather than SATA and are not as large-capacity as 7200 RPM NL-SAS drives.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Given a scenario, select and install storage devices
Question: A technician is installing an M.2 drive and notices the slot is labeled "M.2 2280." What do the numbers 2280 represent?
A) The drive's maximum speed in MB/s
B) The width and length of the module in millimeters
C) The PCIe generation and lane count
D) The SATA revision number
Correct: B
Explanation: M.2 module naming uses the format where the first two digits are the width (22mm) and the remaining digits are the length (80mm), so 2280 is 22mm wide and 80mm long — the most common M.2 size. Other common lengths include 2242 and 2260. The naming does not indicate speed or interface type.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Given a scenario, select and install storage devices
Question: A user needs portable storage to transfer large video files between editing workstations. Which removable storage medium offers the highest capacity and transfer speed for this use case?
A) USB flash drive
B) SD card
C) Optical Blu-ray disc
D) External NVMe SSD via Thunderbolt
Correct: D
Explanation: An external NVMe SSD connected via Thunderbolt 3/4 can achieve speeds exceeding 2,500 MB/s, making it the fastest option for transferring large video files. USB flash drives and SD cards are limited by their NAND controller and USB interface speeds. Blu-ray discs have slow write speeds and relatively limited capacity compared to modern SSDs.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Given a scenario, select and install storage devices
Question: Which storage interface is used by mSATA drives and is now largely replaced by M.2?
A) PCIe x4
B) SATA III
C) IDE
D) USB 3.0
Correct: B
Explanation: mSATA (mini-SATA) drives use the SATA III interface and deliver the same throughput as 2.5-inch SATA SSDs (up to 600 MB/s), just in a smaller form factor. M.2 replaced mSATA because it supports both SATA and NVMe/PCIe interfaces in a more versatile slot. PCIe x4 is used by full-size NVMe add-in cards.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Given a scenario, select and install storage devices
Question: A technician configures four 2 TB drives in RAID 10. What is the total usable storage capacity?
A) 8 TB
B) 6 TB
C) 4 TB
D) 2 TB
Correct: C
Explanation: RAID 10 mirrors pairs of drives and then stripes the mirrors, so exactly half the total raw capacity is usable. With four 2 TB drives (8 TB raw), the usable capacity is 4 TB. RAID 5 with four drives would yield 6 TB (n-1 drives usable). RAID 0 would yield 8 TB but with no redundancy.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Given a scenario, select and install storage devices
Question: A technician is asked to install an optical drive that supports reading and writing to both DVD and Blu-ray media. What type of drive is needed?
A) DVD±RW drive
B) CD-RW drive
C) Blu-ray combo drive
D) BD-RE drive
Correct: C
Explanation: A Blu-ray combo drive reads and writes Blu-ray discs while also supporting DVD and CD read/write, making it the appropriate choice for both disc types. A DVD±RW drive cannot read or write Blu-ray media. A BD-RE drive is a Blu-ray rewritable drive but the term "combo" specifically indicates cross-format read/write capability.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.4 — Given a scenario, install and configure motherboards, CPUs, and add-on cards
Question: Which motherboard form factor measures 12 × 9.6 inches and is the most common standard for full-size desktop builds?
A) Mini-ITX
B) Micro-ATX
C) ATX
D) E-ATX
Correct: C
Explanation: ATX (Advanced Technology eXtended) motherboards measure 12 × 9.6 inches (305 × 244 mm) and are the standard form factor for full-size desktop and tower cases. Micro-ATX is smaller at 9.6 × 9.6 inches. Mini-ITX is even smaller at 6.7 × 6.7 inches, designed for compact builds.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.4 — Given a scenario, install and configure motherboards, CPUs, and add-on cards
Question: A technician is building a home theater PC that must fit in a very small enclosure. Which motherboard form factor is most appropriate?
A) ATX
B) Micro-ATX
C) Mini-ITX
D) E-ATX
Correct: C
Explanation: Mini-ITX measures only 6.7 × 6.7 inches and is designed specifically for compact builds such as home theater PCs and small form factor systems. ATX and Micro-ATX are too large for very small enclosures. E-ATX is even larger than standard ATX and is used for high-end workstation and server builds.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.4 — Given a scenario, install and configure motherboards, CPUs, and add-on cards
Question: Which CPU socket type uses a Land Grid Array (LGA) design where the pins are located on the motherboard socket rather than on the processor?
A) AMD AM5
B) Intel LGA 1700
C) AMD sTRX40
D) Intel BGA
Correct: B
Explanation: Intel uses LGA (Land Grid Array) sockets where the delicate pins are on the motherboard socket and the processor has flat contact pads, protecting the CPU from pin damage. AMD uses PGA (Pin Grid Array) on older sockets like AM4 and has transitioned to LGA with AM5. BGA (Ball Grid Array) is a permanently soldered package used in laptops, not a user-installable socket.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.4 — Given a scenario, install and configure motherboards, CPUs, and add-on cards
Question: A technician powers on a newly built system and gets a single long beep followed by two short beeps. Where should the technician look to decode this POST beep code?
A) The operating system event log
B) The motherboard manual or manufacturer's BIOS documentation
C) The CPU manufacturer's website
D) The Windows Device Manager
Correct: B
Explanation: POST (Power-On Self-Test) beep codes are specific to the BIOS/UEFI manufacturer (AMI, Award, Phoenix) and the motherboard model, so the motherboard manual is the authoritative reference for decoding them. Beep codes indicate hardware-level errors that occur before the OS loads, so event logs and Device Manager are inaccessible at this stage. The CPU manufacturer's site would not document motherboard beep codes.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.4 — Given a scenario, install and configure motherboards, CPUs, and add-on cards
Question: What is the purpose of thermal paste (thermal compound) when installing a CPU cooler?
A) To bond the heatsink permanently to the CPU
B) To fill microscopic air gaps and improve heat transfer between the CPU and heatsink
C) To protect the CPU from electrostatic discharge
D) To lubricate the CPU fan bearings
Correct: B
Explanation: Thermal paste is a thermally conductive compound applied between the CPU integrated heat spreader and the heatsink base to fill microscopic surface imperfections and eliminate air gaps, which are poor heat conductors. It does not create a permanent bond — heatsinks can be removed after application. Thermal paste has no ESD protection or lubricating properties.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.4 — Given a scenario, install and configure motherboards, CPUs, and add-on cards
Question: A workstation needs to capture HDMI video input from a game console for streaming. Which type of expansion card should be installed?
A) Sound card
B) Network interface card (NIC)
C) Video capture card
D) GPU
Correct: C
Explanation: A video capture card has HDMI or other video input connectors that receive an external video signal and pass it to the CPU/GPU for processing, recording, or streaming. A GPU outputs video signals but does not accept external video input in consumer configurations. A sound card handles audio processing, and a NIC handles network connectivity.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.4 — Given a scenario, install and configure motherboards, CPUs, and add-on cards
Question: Which BIOS/UEFI feature stores cryptographic keys and can be used to support BitLocker drive encryption on a Windows system?
A) Secure Boot
B) TPM (Trusted Platform Module)
C) UEFI CSM
D) XMP profile
Correct: B
Explanation: TPM (Trusted Platform Module) is a dedicated security chip or firmware component that stores cryptographic keys, certificates, and passwords in a tamper-resistant manner, and is required for Windows 11 and BitLocker encryption. Secure Boot verifies the bootloader's digital signature but does not store encryption keys. XMP is a memory overclocking profile.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.4 — Given a scenario, install and configure motherboards, CPUs, and add-on cards
Question: A technician needs to install a high-end GPU that requires an x16 PCIe slot. The motherboard has slots labeled x1, x4, x8, and x16. Which slot should the GPU be installed in?
A) PCIe x1
B) PCIe x4
C) PCIe x8
D) PCIe x16
Correct: D
Explanation: High-end GPUs require the full bandwidth of a PCIe x16 slot to prevent a performance bottleneck, as they are designed to use all 16 lanes. While a GPU can physically fit in an x8 or x4 slot (if open-ended), the reduced lane count limits bandwidth. PCIe x1 slots are too short to physically seat a full-size GPU.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.4 — Given a scenario, install and configure motherboards, CPUs, and add-on cards
Question: Which cooling method circulates liquid through a water block mounted on the CPU to transfer heat to a radiator with fans?
A) Heat pipe passive cooling
B) All-in-one (AIO) liquid cooling
C) Phase-change cooling
D) Vapor chamber cooling
Correct: B
Explanation: AIO (All-in-One) liquid cooling systems use a pump in the CPU water block to circulate coolant through sealed tubing to a radiator mounted in the case, where fans dissipate the heat. Heat pipes are sealed passive devices used in heatsinks that use evaporation/condensation internally. Phase-change cooling uses a compressor and refrigerant like an air conditioner.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.4 — Given a scenario, install and configure motherboards, CPUs, and add-on cards
Question: A user wants to use an older operating system that requires legacy BIOS boot mode, but the motherboard only shows UEFI in its settings. What feature allows UEFI firmware to support legacy BIOS boot?
A) Secure Boot
B) Fast Boot
C) CSM (Compatibility Support Module)
D) TPM 2.0
Correct: C
Explanation: CSM (Compatibility Support Module) is a UEFI feature that emulates a legacy BIOS environment, allowing older operating systems and bootloaders that do not support UEFI to boot. Secure Boot is a UEFI security feature that verifies boot software signatures. Fast Boot reduces POST time by skipping some hardware checks.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.4 — Given a scenario, install and configure motherboards, CPUs, and add-on cards
Question: What is the function of a chipset on a motherboard?
A) To provide primary processing power for application software
B) To manage communication between the CPU, memory, and peripherals
C) To store the BIOS/UEFI firmware
D) To regulate voltage delivered to the CPU
Correct: B
Explanation: The chipset acts as the traffic controller on a motherboard, managing data flow between the CPU, RAM, storage controllers, USB controllers, PCIe slots, and other peripherals. The CPU handles application processing. BIOS/UEFI is stored in a separate flash memory chip. Voltage regulation is handled by the VRM (Voltage Regulator Module).

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.4 — Given a scenario, install and configure motherboards, CPUs, and add-on cards
Question: A technician installs a new sound card but Windows does not recognize it. The device shows an exclamation mark in Device Manager. What is the most likely first step to resolve this?
A) Replace the PCIe slot
B) Install the correct driver for the sound card
C) Enable Secure Boot in UEFI
D) Reseat the CPU
Correct: B
Explanation: An exclamation mark in Device Manager typically indicates a driver issue — the hardware is detected but lacks a proper driver for Windows to use it. Installing the manufacturer's driver for the sound card resolves this in most cases. Secure Boot and CPU reseating would not affect device driver recognition, and PCIe slots rarely fail.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.5 — Given a scenario, install or replace the appropriate power supply
Question: Which PSU connector provides the primary power to an ATX motherboard and has 24 pins?
A) EPS 8-pin
B) 24-pin ATX main connector
C) PCIe 8-pin
D) Molex 4-pin
Correct: B
Explanation: The 24-pin ATX main power connector (evolved from the original 20-pin connector) is the primary power connection to the motherboard, providing multiple voltage rails including +3.3V, +5V, and +12V. The EPS 8-pin connector provides additional +12V power specifically to the CPU. The PCIe 6/8-pin connectors power discrete graphics cards.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.5 — Given a scenario, install or replace the appropriate power supply
Question: A technician is installing a high-end CPU in a workstation motherboard. The CPU power connector slot on the motherboard has 8 pins. What cable from the PSU is needed?
A) 24-pin ATX
B) PCIe 6-pin
C) EPS 8-pin (or 4+4-pin)
D) SATA power
Correct: C
Explanation: The EPS (Entry-Level Power Supply) 8-pin connector (also available as a 4+4-pin split cable for compatibility) provides dedicated +12V power to the CPU voltage regulator. The 24-pin ATX connector powers the motherboard but does not supply adequate current for the CPU alone. PCIe connectors power graphics cards, not CPUs.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.5 — Given a scenario, install or replace the appropriate power supply
Question: A user in Europe needs to connect a US-purchased computer to the local power grid. What voltage difference must be addressed?
A) 12V vs 5V
B) 110V vs 220V
C) 60 Hz vs 50 Hz
D) AC vs DC conversion
Correct: B
Explanation: The US uses 110-120V AC power while Europe uses 220-240V AC, a significant voltage difference that can damage a non-universal PSU. Many modern PSUs have auto-sensing universal voltage capability, but older units may require a manual voltage selector switch to be set correctly. Operating a 110V PSU on 220V without proper adjustment can destroy the power supply and connected components.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.5 — Given a scenario, install or replace the appropriate power supply
Question: Which type of PSU allows the user to attach only the cables needed for their build, reducing cable clutter?
A) Non-modular PSU
B) Semi-modular PSU
C) Fully modular PSU
D) Passive PSU
Correct: C
Explanation: A fully modular PSU has no permanently attached cables — all cables connect via sockets on the PSU itself, so only the cables actually needed are installed. A non-modular PSU has all cables permanently attached. A semi-modular PSU has essential cables (24-pin, EPS) permanently attached with additional cables being removable.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.5 — Given a scenario, install or replace the appropriate power supply
Question: A discrete GPU requires a PCIe 8-pin power connector. The technician's PSU only has a PCIe 6-pin connector. What should be done?
A) Use the 6-pin connector; the GPU will use the available pins
B) Use a PCIe 6-pin to 8-pin adapter cable
C) Use two SATA power connectors bridged together
D) Connect the GPU to the 24-pin ATX connector instead
Correct: B
Explanation: PCIe 6-to-8-pin adapter cables are commonly included with GPUs or PSUs to allow a 6-pin source to connect to an 8-pin GPU connector, though this should only be used within the wattage limits of the PSU and connector. Using only a 6-pin on an 8-pin connector can cause the GPU to throttle or fail to operate. SATA-to-PCIe adapters exist but are considered fire hazards under high load.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.5 — Given a scenario, install or replace the appropriate power supply
Question: A technician is calculating PSU requirements for a system with a CPU rated at 125W, a GPU rated at 250W, and other components totaling 100W. What minimum PSU wattage should be selected?
A) 475W
B) 550W
C) 650W
D) 350W
Correct: C
Explanation: The total component power draw is 475W, but PSUs should be sized with a 20-30% headroom for efficiency and longevity, bringing the recommended minimum to approximately 570-615W. A 650W PSU provides adequate headroom and keeps the PSU operating in its most efficient range (typically 50-80% load). A 475W or 550W PSU would be running near its maximum capacity under load.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.5 — Given a scenario, install or replace the appropriate power supply
Question: Which PSU connector uses a 4-pin design with yellow (+12V), black (ground), red (+5V), and black wires and was historically used for IDE hard drives and optical drives?
A) SATA power connector
B) EPS 4-pin
C) Molex 4-pin
D) Berg connector
Correct: C
Explanation: The Molex 4-pin peripheral connector has been used for decades to power IDE hard drives, optical drives, and case fans, providing +12V and +5V rails. SATA power connectors use a 15-pin flat connector. EPS 4-pin connectors are used for CPU power. Berg connectors are the smaller 4-pin floppy drive connectors.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.5 — Given a scenario, install or replace the appropriate power supply
Question: A data center requires that servers continue operating if a single power supply fails. Which PSU feature fulfills this requirement?
A) Modular cabling
B) 80 Plus certification
C) Redundant power supply (hot-swap)
D) High wattage single-rail design
Correct: C
Explanation: Redundant hot-swap power supplies allow a failed PSU to be removed and replaced while the server continues operating, using the second PSU to carry the full load. 80 Plus certification indicates power efficiency ratings but provides no fault tolerance. Modular cabling reduces clutter but does not provide redundancy.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.5 — Given a scenario, install or replace the appropriate power supply
Question: What does 80 Plus Gold certification indicate about a power supply?
A) It can output 80W of power guaranteed
B) It operates at 87-90% efficiency at 20%, 50%, and 100% loads
C) It has gold-plated connectors for reliability
D) It uses a single +12V rail architecture
Correct: B
Explanation: 80 Plus Gold certification means the PSU achieves at least 87% efficiency at 20% load and 90% efficiency at 50% load, reducing wasted energy as heat. The certification has nothing to do with connector materials or output wattage limits. Higher tiers (Platinum, Titanium) achieve even greater efficiency percentages.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.5 — Given a scenario, install or replace the appropriate power supply
Question: A technician notices a system randomly powers off under heavy gaming load but operates normally under light use. What component is most likely failing?
A) RAM module
B) CPU thermal paste
C) Power supply unit
D) GPU driver
Correct: C
Explanation: Random shutdowns specifically under heavy load are a classic symptom of an underpowered or failing PSU that cannot maintain stable voltage rails under peak demand. Thermal paste degradation would cause thermal throttling before shutdown and would affect all workloads. RAM failures typically manifest as blue screens or memory errors, not load-dependent power cutoffs.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.6 — Given a scenario, deploy and configure multifunction devices/printers and settings
Question: Which printer technology uses a laser beam to create an electrostatic image on a photosensitive drum, which then attracts toner powder?
A) Inkjet
B) Thermal
C) Laser
D) Impact
Correct: C
Explanation: Laser printers use a laser to discharge specific areas of a charged photosensitive drum, creating an electrostatic pattern that attracts oppositely charged toner particles, which are then fused to paper with heat. Inkjet printers spray liquid ink droplets through microscopic nozzles. Thermal printers use heat-sensitive paper or a thermal printhead to apply ink.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.6 — Given a scenario, deploy and configure multifunction devices/printers and settings
Question: A receipt printer at a retail store uses heat-sensitive paper and has no ink cartridges. Which printer type is this?
A) Inkjet
B) Laser
C) Impact
D) Thermal
Correct: D
Explanation: Thermal printers use a heated printhead to activate heat-sensitive coating on special paper, producing images without ink cartridges or ribbons. They are widely used for receipts, shipping labels, and tickets due to their speed and low maintenance. Inkjet and laser printers require ink or toner consumables.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.6 — Given a scenario, deploy and configure multifunction devices/printers and settings
Question: A printing environment requires hard-copy forms with multiple carbon copies simultaneously. Which printer type is required?
A) Laser
B) Inkjet
C) Thermal
D) Impact (dot matrix)
Correct: D
Explanation: Impact printers (dot matrix) use a print head with pins that physically strike an ink ribbon against the paper, creating impressions that can pass through multiple carbon copy layers simultaneously. No other printer technology can create carbon copies because they require physical pressure. Laser and inkjet print only the top sheet.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.6 — Given a scenario, deploy and configure multifunction devices/printers and settings
Question: A user wants to print on both sides of each page automatically without manually flipping the paper. Which printer feature is needed?
A) Collating
B) Duplex printing
C) Orientation setting
D) Print quality selection
Correct: B
Explanation: Duplex printing (automatic double-sided printing) allows the printer to print on both sides of the paper automatically using a duplexer mechanism. Collating determines the order of pages in a multi-page print job. Orientation controls whether the page prints in portrait or landscape.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.6 — Given a scenario, deploy and configure multifunction devices/printers and settings
Question: A small office needs to share a single printer among five Windows computers without a dedicated print server. What is the simplest method to accomplish this?
A) Configure each computer with a unique static IP for the printer
B) Enable printer sharing on the computer connected to the printer
