C) Install a network card in the printer
D) Purchase five separate printers
Correct: B
Explanation: Windows printer sharing allows the computer hosting the printer via USB to share it over the network, so other computers on the same network can connect to and print through the host computer. This requires the host computer to be powered on when others need to print. A network card in the printer would make it a direct network printer, which is a valid but more complex and expensive solution.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.6 — Given a scenario, deploy and configure multifunction devices/printers and settings
Question: A multifunction printer (MFP) is connected to the network. A user wants to scan a document and send it directly to an email address. Which MFP feature enables this?
A) Fax over IP
B) Scan to email
C) Pull printing
D) Cloud print
Correct: B
Explanation: Scan to email is a built-in MFP feature that scans a document and sends it as an email attachment using a configured SMTP server, allowing users to digitize and distribute documents without first sending to a computer. Fax over IP sends faxes over internet connections. Pull printing holds jobs in a queue until authenticated at the printer.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.6 — Given a scenario, deploy and configure multifunction devices/printers and settings
Question: After replacing a laser printer's toner cartridge, prints show faint horizontal lines at regular intervals across the page. What component is most likely causing this?
A) Fuser assembly
B) Transfer belt
C) Imaging drum
D) Pickup roller
Correct: C
Explanation: Regular horizontal bands or lines repeating at intervals corresponding to the drum circumference indicate a damaged or worn imaging (photosensitive) drum that is not holding the electrostatic charge uniformly. The fuser assembly causes issues like toner smearing or not fusing. Pickup roller problems cause paper feed failures.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.6 — Given a scenario, deploy and configure multifunction devices/printers and settings
Question: A 3D printer uses spools of plastic filament that is melted and deposited layer by layer. Which 3D printing technology is this?
A) Stereolithography (SLA)
B) Selective Laser Sintering (SLS)
C) Fused Deposition Modeling (FDM)
D) Digital Light Processing (DLP)
Correct: C
Explanation: FDM (Fused Deposition Modeling) is the most common consumer 3D printing technology, using a heated nozzle to melt plastic filament (PLA, ABS, PETG) and deposit it layer by layer. SLA uses a UV laser to cure liquid photopolymer resin. SLS uses a laser to sinter powdered material without a liquid binder.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.6 — Given a scenario, deploy and configure multifunction devices/printers and settings
Question: A user prints a test page successfully but cannot print from any application. Documents appear in the print queue and then disappear without printing. What is the most likely cause?
A) The printer is out of toner
B) The printer driver is corrupted or incompatible
C) The paper tray is empty
D) The printer IP address has changed
Correct: B
Explanation: When test pages print successfully but application-generated jobs disappear from the queue without output, a corrupted or incompatible printer driver is the most common cause, as the driver handles translation of application print data. A toner or paper issue would also prevent the test page from printing. If the IP changed, the printer would be offline and no jobs would be sent.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.6 — Given a scenario, deploy and configure multifunction devices/printers and settings
Question: A network printer is assigned an IP address by DHCP and its IP address changes frequently, disrupting printing for all users. What is the best solution?
A) Reinstall printer drivers on all computers weekly
B) Assign the printer a static IP address or DHCP reservation
C) Connect the printer via USB to each workstation
D) Disable the printer's wireless adapter
Correct: B
Explanation: Assigning a static IP address or creating a DHCP reservation ties a fixed IP to the printer's MAC address so it never changes, eliminating the need to reconfigure client computers. Reinstalling drivers is a workaround, not a solution. USB connections would not scale for a shared network printer environment.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.7 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: Which cloud service model provides virtualized computing infrastructure (servers, storage, networking) over the internet, where the customer manages the OS and applications?
A) SaaS
B) PaaS
C) IaaS
D) DaaS
Correct: C
Explanation: IaaS (Infrastructure as a Service) provides raw computing infrastructure — virtual machines, storage, and networking — that the customer manages from the OS level up. PaaS provides a development platform where the provider manages the OS and middleware. SaaS delivers fully managed applications accessible via a web browser.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.7 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: A development team needs a platform to build and deploy web applications without managing the underlying servers or OS. Which cloud model is most appropriate?
A) IaaS
B) PaaS
C) SaaS
D) Private cloud
Correct: B
Explanation: PaaS (Platform as a Service) provides a managed environment including the OS, runtime, and middleware, allowing developers to focus on writing and deploying code without managing infrastructure. IaaS requires the team to manage the OS and server configuration. SaaS provides finished applications rather than a development platform.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.7 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: Microsoft 365 and Google Workspace are examples of which cloud service model?
A) IaaS
B) PaaS
C) SaaS
D) CaaS
Correct: C
Explanation: SaaS (Software as a Service) delivers fully functional applications over the internet that users access through a browser or thin client, with the provider managing everything from infrastructure to the application itself. Microsoft 365 and Google Workspace provide email, documents, and collaboration tools as a service. IaaS and PaaS are lower-level cloud models requiring more customer management.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.7 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: Which cloud deployment model is owned and operated exclusively by a single organization and hosted either on-premises or by a third party?
A) Public cloud
B) Hybrid cloud
C) Community cloud
D) Private cloud
Correct: D
Explanation: A private cloud is dedicated to a single organization, providing greater control, security, and customization compared to public cloud services. A public cloud is shared infrastructure available to any paying customer. A hybrid cloud combines public and private cloud environments. A community cloud is shared among organizations with common requirements.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.7 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: A company uses AWS for some workloads while maintaining on-premises servers for sensitive data. Which cloud deployment model describes this arrangement?
A) Public cloud
B) Private cloud
C) Hybrid cloud
D) Community cloud
Correct: C
Explanation: A hybrid cloud combines on-premises or private cloud resources with public cloud services, allowing organizations to keep sensitive workloads in-house while leveraging public cloud scalability for other tasks. A public cloud uses entirely third-party infrastructure. A community cloud is shared among multiple organizations with shared concerns.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.7 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: Which cloud characteristic allows a user to automatically provision computing resources as needed without requiring human interaction from the service provider?
A) Measured service
B) Rapid elasticity
C) On-demand self-service
D) Resource pooling
Correct: C
Explanation: On-demand self-service is the cloud characteristic that allows users to provision resources (virtual machines, storage, bandwidth) automatically through a portal or API without needing to contact the provider. Measured service (metered utilization) tracks resource consumption for billing. Rapid elasticity refers to the ability to quickly scale resources up or down.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.7 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: Which cloud characteristic describes the provider's ability to serve multiple customers using the same physical infrastructure while keeping each customer's data logically separated?
A) On-demand self-service
B) Resource pooling
C) Rapid elasticity
D) Broad network access
Correct: B
Explanation: Resource pooling means the provider uses a multi-tenant model to serve multiple customers from the same shared physical resources (compute, storage, network), with logical isolation between tenants. Rapid elasticity is the ability to scale resources quickly. Broad network access means services are available over the network via standard client devices.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.7 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: A company's cloud provider charges based on the exact amount of CPU time, storage, and bandwidth consumed each month. Which cloud characteristic is being applied?
A) Rapid elasticity
B) Resource pooling
C) On-demand self-service
D) Measured service (metered utilization)
Correct: D
Explanation: Measured service (metered utilization) means cloud resource usage is monitored, controlled, and reported, enabling the pay-as-you-go billing model where customers pay only for what they consume. Rapid elasticity refers to scaling capacity. Resource pooling refers to shared physical infrastructure serving multiple tenants.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.7 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: Several healthcare organizations share a cloud environment built specifically to meet HIPAA compliance requirements. Which cloud deployment model is this?
A) Private cloud
B) Public cloud
C) Hybrid cloud
D) Community cloud
Correct: D
Explanation: A community cloud is shared infrastructure used by organizations that have common concerns such as regulatory compliance, security requirements, or mission. Healthcare organizations sharing HIPAA-compliant infrastructure is a textbook community cloud example. A private cloud serves only one organization. A public cloud is open to any customer and may not meet specific regulatory needs.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.7 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: Which cloud characteristic describes the ability to quickly increase or decrease compute resources in response to changing demand?
A) On-demand self-service
B) Measured service
C) Rapid elasticity
D) Broad network access
Correct: C
Explanation: Rapid elasticity allows cloud resources to be provisioned and released quickly — sometimes automatically — to match demand, appearing as unlimited capacity to the user. On-demand self-service is the ability to provision without provider intervention. Measured service refers to metered usage billing.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: A technician needs to connect a new monitor that supports 144 Hz refresh rate at 2560x1440 resolution. Which cable interface can reliably support this without an adapter?
A) VGA
B) DVI-D Single Link
C) DisplayPort 1.2
D) HDMI 1.4
Correct: C
Explanation: DisplayPort 1.2 supports bandwidth sufficient for 2560x1440 at 144 Hz (QHD 144 Hz), making it the appropriate choice. HDMI 1.4 is limited to 1080p at 120 Hz or 4K at 30 Hz. DVI-D Single Link supports only up to 1920x1200 at 60 Hz. VGA is analog and cannot support high refresh rates at modern resolutions.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: What is the maximum length of a standard USB 2.0 cable without a signal repeater?
A) 3 meters
B) 5 meters
C) 10 meters
D) 1 meter
Correct: B
Explanation: The USB 2.0 specification defines a maximum cable length of 5 meters (approximately 16.4 feet) before signal degradation exceeds acceptable limits. USB 3.0 cables have a shorter maximum length of about 3 meters. Active USB extension cables or hubs can be used to extend the distance beyond these limits.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: Which connector is found on the device end of a standard USB cable connecting a printer or scanner to a computer?
A) USB-A
B) USB-B
C) USB-C
D) USB Micro-A
Correct: B
Explanation: USB-B (Type-B) is the square-shaped connector used on the device end (printers, scanners, hubs) of a standard USB cable, while USB-A connects to the host computer. USB-C is a newer reversible connector replacing both USB-A and USB-B in newer devices. USB Micro-A is a specialized connector for OTG applications.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Given a scenario, install the appropriate RAM
Question: A technician is installing RAM in a server that must correct single-bit errors automatically during operation. The server motherboard supports ECC. Which modules should be purchased?
A) DDR4 non-ECC unbuffered (UDIMM)
B) DDR4 ECC registered (RDIMM)
C) DDR4 SO-DIMM
D) DDR5 non-ECC
Correct: B
Explanation: Server environments requiring ECC and high memory capacity use Registered (Buffered) DIMMs (RDIMMs), which include a register chip between the memory controller and the DRAM chips, improving signal integrity at high capacities. Unbuffered ECC DIMMs exist but are limited in capacity and channel count. SO-DIMMs are for laptops, not servers.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Given a scenario, install the appropriate RAM
Question: A user reports that after installing new RAM, the system only recognizes half the installed capacity. The new sticks are installed in slots 1 and 2 instead of the recommended slots 2 and 4. What should the technician do?
A) Replace the RAM modules
B) Move the RAM to the correct dual-channel slots as specified in the motherboard manual
C) Update the BIOS to recognize the new RAM
D) Enable XMP in BIOS settings
Correct: B
Explanation: Most dual-channel motherboards require DIMMs to be installed in specific slots (often color-coded) to enable dual-channel mode; installing in adjacent slots 1 and 2 instead of 1 and 3 (or 2 and 4) may result in single-channel operation or only partial recognition. The motherboard manual specifies the correct slot population order. XMP enables overclocking profiles, not dual-channel mode.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Given a scenario, select and install storage devices
Question: An NVMe SSD in a workstation shows an M.2 key type of "M." The motherboard has an M.2 slot with an "M" key. Which statement about this installation is correct?
A) The drive will not fit because the key types don't match
B) The M-keyed slot supports NVMe PCIe drives and the installation is correct
C) An adapter is needed to convert M-key to B-key
D) M-key slots only support SATA M.2 drives
Correct: B
Explanation: The M key (single notch on the right side) is used for NVMe PCIe M.2 drives and is the correct slot for NVMe SSDs. B+M keyed drives have notches on both sides and fit in either B-key or M-key slots but typically run SATA. An M-keyed drive and M-keyed slot are a matching, compatible combination requiring no adapter.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Given a scenario, select and install storage devices
Question: A RAID 5 array consists of five 4 TB drives. One drive fails and is replaced. During the rebuild, a second drive fails. What is the result?
A) The array rebuilds using the parity from the remaining drives
B) The array continues operating in degraded mode
C) All data on the array is lost
D) The second failed drive's data is preserved on the hot spare
Correct: C
Explanation: RAID 5 can tolerate only a single drive failure at a time; a second drive failure during rebuild results in complete data loss because parity information from the first failed drive is still being reconstructed. This is why the rebuild window on large drives is considered a risk period. RAID 6 tolerates two simultaneous failures using dual parity.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.4 — Given a scenario, install and configure motherboards, CPUs, and add-on cards
Question: A technician is building a compact workstation using a Mini-ITX motherboard. How many PCIe expansion slots does a standard Mini-ITX board typically provide?
A) None
B) One
C) Two
D) Four
Correct: B
Explanation: Due to its compact 6.7 × 6.7-inch size, a Mini-ITX motherboard typically provides only one PCIe expansion slot (usually x16 for a GPU). ATX boards can accommodate up to seven expansion slots. This limitation is a key trade-off when choosing Mini-ITX for space-constrained builds.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.4 — Given a scenario, install and configure motherboards, CPUs, and add-on cards
Question: A workstation's BIOS does not recognize an NVMe SSD installed in the M.2 slot. The drive is known to be functional. What BIOS setting should the technician check?
A) Secure Boot mode
B) TPM configuration
C) M.2 slot PCIe/NVMe mode vs. SATA mode
D) Memory XMP profile
Correct: C
Explanation: Some M.2 slots can operate in either SATA or PCIe/NVMe mode, and the BIOS may need to be configured to recognize an NVMe drive if the default mode is set to SATA. Secure Boot and TPM settings do not affect drive detection during POST. XMP is a memory overclocking setting unrelated to storage detection.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.4 — Given a scenario, install and configure motherboards, CPUs, and add-on cards
Question: A technician applies too much thermal paste to a CPU and the excess spreads onto the motherboard socket. What is the most likely consequence?
A) Improved heat dissipation
B) Potential short circuits from conductive thermal paste bridging contacts
C) The CPU will run at lower clock speeds
D) The heatsink will not seat properly due to excess thickness
Correct: B
Explanation: Many thermal pastes contain metallic particles (silver-based compounds) that can conduct electricity; if such paste contacts the CPU socket pins or surrounding circuitry, it can cause short circuits. Non-conductive pastes are safer if spread occurs, but all excess paste should be cleaned immediately. Too much paste also creates a thicker thermal barrier that can actually worsen heat transfer.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.5 — Given a scenario, install or replace the appropriate power supply
Question: A technician replaces a PSU in a system, but after installation the system powers on for 2 seconds then shuts off. What should the technician check first?
A) Whether the 24-pin ATX connector is fully seated on the motherboard
B) Whether the case fans are spinning
C) Whether the monitor is connected
D) Whether the hard drive is recognized
Correct: A
Explanation: A system that powers on briefly then immediately shuts off often has an improperly seated ATX main power connector, causing the motherboard to detect a power fault. This is one of the first checks after a PSU replacement. Monitor connection and HDD recognition would not cause an immediate power cutoff, and fans spinning indicates the system did receive power momentarily.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.6 — Given a scenario, deploy and configure multifunction devices/printers and settings
Question: A laser printer produces output with toner that smears when touched immediately after printing. Which component is most likely defective?
A) Imaging drum
B) Toner cartridge
C) Fuser assembly
D) Transfer corona wire
Correct: C
Explanation: The fuser assembly uses heat and pressure rollers to permanently bond toner to the paper; if the fuser is defective or not reaching operating temperature, toner will not be fused and will smear when touched. An imaging drum problem causes banding or ghost images. A toner cartridge issue causes light or missing output, not smearing.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.6 — Given a scenario, deploy and configure multifunction devices/printers and settings
Question: A user prints a 50-page document and the pages come out in reverse order (page 50 first). Which print setting controls the order pages are output?
A) Duplex
B) Orientation
C) Collation
D) Print quality
Correct: C
Explanation: Collation settings control whether multi-page and multi-copy documents are assembled in the correct page order. Printing in reverse order is a collation issue, often correctable by selecting "Reverse page order" or adjusting the collation option in the printer properties. Duplex controls double-sided printing, and orientation controls portrait vs. landscape.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.7 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: A company's cloud infrastructure automatically provisions additional web server instances during peak traffic and removes them when demand drops. Which cloud characteristic is this?
A) Measured service
B) On-demand self-service
C) Rapid elasticity
D) Resource pooling
Correct: C
Explanation: Rapid elasticity is the cloud capability that allows resources to be provisioned and released quickly — often automatically — to align with workload demand, appearing to the user as limitless capacity. Measured service tracks usage for billing. On-demand self-service is user-initiated provisioning without provider assistance.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: A technician is installing network cable in a building and needs to run it vertically between floors through the building's internal pathways. Which cable rating is required for this vertical run?
A) Plenum
B) PVC
C) Riser
D) Direct burial
Correct: C
Explanation: Riser-rated cable (CMR) is designed for vertical runs between floors through conduit or cable risers and has fire-retardant properties to prevent flames from spreading between floors. Plenum cable is required for air-handling spaces and exceeds riser requirements. Direct burial cable is designed for underground outdoor runs.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: Which USB version introduced the blue-colored Type-A connector to visually distinguish it from USB 2.0 ports on devices?
A) USB 1.1
B) USB 2.0
C) USB 3.0
D) USB 4.0
Correct: C
Explanation: USB 3.0 introduced the blue color coding for Type-A connectors and ports to help users visually distinguish SuperSpeed USB 3.0 ports from the older black or white USB 2.0 ports. USB 4.0 uses the USB-C connector form factor. USB 1.1 ports were typically white or gray.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Given a scenario, install the appropriate RAM
Question: A technician needs to install RAM into a system where the CPU has a dual-channel memory controller and the motherboard has four slots. For maximum performance, how many sticks and in which configuration should be installed?
A) One stick in slot 1
B) Two sticks of the same capacity in the dual-channel slots (e.g., A1 and B1)
C) Three sticks in slots 1, 2, and 3
D) Four sticks of different capacities
Correct: B
Explanation: To activate dual-channel mode with a four-slot motherboard, two identical capacity sticks should be installed in the manufacturer-specified paired slots (typically A1/B1 or A2/B2, often color-coded), which doubles the effective memory bus width to 128 bits. Odd numbers of sticks cannot form symmetric channel pairs. Mixed-capacity configurations may fall back to single-channel or flex mode.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Given a scenario, select and install storage devices
Question: A storage administrator wants to implement a RAID configuration that can sustain two simultaneous drive failures across a six-drive array. Which RAID level provides this tolerance?
A) RAID 5
B) RAID 6
C) RAID 10
D) RAID 1
Correct: B
Explanation: RAID 6 uses dual distributed parity, allowing the array to sustain any two simultaneous drive failures without data loss, making it suitable for large arrays where the risk of a second failure during rebuild is significant. RAID 5 tolerates only a single drive failure. RAID 10 can tolerate multiple failures only if they are not both drives in the same mirrored pair.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Given a scenario, select and install storage devices
Question: A content creation studio needs storage with the highest sequential write performance for recording uncompressed 4K video. Which option is best?
A) 5400 RPM 3.5-inch HDD RAID 1
B) 7200 RPM HDD RAID 5
C) NVMe SSD RAID 0
D) SATA SSD single drive
Correct: C
Explanation: NVMe SSDs in RAID 0 stripe data across multiple drives, combining the high sequential throughput of NVMe (3,500+ MB/s per drive) to achieve maximum write speeds needed for uncompressed 4K video. SATA SSDs and HDDs cannot match NVMe's sequential performance. RAID 1 and RAID 5 with HDDs would be far below the bandwidth requirements for uncompressed 4K.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.4 — Given a scenario, install and configure motherboards, CPUs, and add-on cards
Question: An HSM (Hardware Security Module) in an enterprise environment serves what primary purpose?
A) Monitoring CPU temperatures and fan speeds
B) Storing and managing cryptographic keys in a tamper-resistant device
C) Providing hardware-level RAID functionality
D) Filtering network traffic at the hardware level
Correct: B
Explanation: An HSM (Hardware Security Module) is a physical device dedicated to securely generating, storing, and managing cryptographic keys and performing cryptographic operations in a tamper-resistant, certified environment. Unlike software key storage, HSMs provide physical protection against key extraction. RAID controllers and temperature monitoring are handled by separate hardware components.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.4 — Given a scenario, install and configure motherboards, CPUs, and add-on cards
Question: A technician configures UEFI Secure Boot on a new workstation. What does Secure Boot prevent?
A) Unauthorized users from changing BIOS settings
B) Unsigned or untrusted bootloaders and OS kernels from loading
C) The system from booting from USB drives
D) Overclocking of the CPU beyond rated specifications
Correct: B
Explanation: Secure Boot is a UEFI feature that verifies the digital signatures of bootloaders and OS kernels against a database of trusted certificates, preventing malware, rootkits, and unsigned software from loading during the boot process. It does not prevent USB booting by itself (boot order settings do that). Password-protecting UEFI settings is a separate security feature.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.5 — Given a scenario, install or replace the appropriate power supply
Question: A technician is installing a SATA SSD in a desktop that currently only has Molex connectors available from the PSU. What is needed to connect the SSD?
A) A SATA to Molex power adapter cable
B) A Molex to SATA power adapter cable
C) An additional PSU
D) A PCIe to SATA power cable
Correct: B
Explanation: A Molex-to-SATA power adapter converts the 4-pin Molex peripheral connector output to the 15-pin SATA power connector required by SATA drives. Note the direction matters — converting Molex (source) to SATA (destination). Using a SATA-to-Molex cable in the opposite direction would require a SATA power source, which the PSU doesn't provide.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.6 — Given a scenario, deploy and configure multifunction devices/printers and settings
Question: A user prints a landscape-oriented spreadsheet but the output is cut off on the right side. Which print setting needs to be adjusted?
A) Paper quality
B) Collation
C) Page orientation
D) Print resolution
Correct: C
Explanation: Changing the page orientation from portrait to landscape in the print settings ensures the printer formats the output to match the document's horizontal layout, preventing cutoff. Collation affects page ordering in multi-copy jobs. Resolution affects print quality, not how content fits on the page.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.6 — Given a scenario, deploy and configure multifunction devices/printers and settings
Question: Which printing method places inkjet cartridges in the printer and works by heating ink to create bubbles that force droplets onto the page?
A) Continuous ink tank
B) Thermal inkjet
C) Piezoelectric inkjet
D) Solid ink
Correct: B
Explanation: Thermal inkjet technology (used in Canon and HP printers) uses tiny resistors to superheat ink, creating a vapor bubble that forces a droplet through the nozzle onto the paper. Piezoelectric inkjet (used in Epson printers) uses electrically stimulated crystals to eject ink without heat. Continuous ink tank printers use reservoirs rather than cartridges but still use one of these methods.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.7 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: An organization uses Amazon Web Services (AWS) for cloud computing. AWS is an example of which cloud deployment model?
A) Private cloud
B) Community cloud
C) Public cloud
D) Hybrid cloud
Correct: C
Explanation: AWS, Microsoft Azure, and Google Cloud Platform are public cloud providers that offer shared infrastructure to any paying customer over the internet. A private cloud is exclusively used by a single organization. A hybrid cloud combines on-premises or private cloud with a public cloud provider.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: A technician needs to connect a laptop's USB-C port to an older projector with only a VGA input. What is required?
A) No adapter is needed; USB-C natively supports VGA
B) A USB-C to VGA adapter or dock
C) A DisplayPort to HDMI cable
D) A Thunderbolt to DVI adapter
Correct: B
Explanation: USB-C does not natively output VGA signals, requiring an active USB-C to VGA adapter that converts the digital DisplayPort Alt Mode signal to the analog VGA format. Thunderbolt 3/4 also uses USB-C and can use the same adapters. A DisplayPort-to-HDMI cable would not help connect to a VGA projector.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: Cat 5e cable is rated for which maximum Ethernet speed over 100 meters?
A) 100 Mbps
B) 1 Gbps
C) 10 Gbps
D) 2.5 Gbps
Correct: B
Explanation: Cat 5e (Category 5 enhanced) is rated for 1000BASE-T (Gigabit Ethernet) over 100 meters, using all four wire pairs with crosstalk improvements over original Cat 5. Cat 5e cannot reliably support 10 Gbps at full 100-meter distances. Cat 6 introduced improved shielding and twist rates for 10 Gbps support.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Given a scenario, install the appropriate RAM
Question: A motherboard has a maximum RAM capacity of 64 GB across four DDR4 slots. The user wants to maximize memory while remaining under this limit. Which RAM configuration achieves this?
A) Four sticks of 8 GB
B) Two sticks of 16 GB
C) Four sticks of 16 GB
D) Two sticks of 32 GB
Correct: C
Explanation: Four sticks of 16 GB = 64 GB total, exactly reaching the motherboard's maximum capacity while using all four slots for potential dual-channel operation across both channel pairs. Two sticks of 32 GB also equals 64 GB but leaves two slots empty; while functional, four sticks can improve bandwidth on boards that support it. Four sticks of 8 GB is only 32 GB.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Given a scenario, select and install storage devices
Question: A system builder is creating a budget gaming PC and wants to use two SSDs — one for the OS and one for game storage. The motherboard has one M.2 slot and two SATA ports. What is the most cost-effective configuration?
A) Two NVMe M.2 SSDs
B) One NVMe M.2 SSD for the OS and one SATA SSD for game storage
C) Two SATA HDDs
D) One SATA SSD for the OS and one HDD for games
Correct: B
Explanation: Using an NVMe M.2 SSD for the OS provides fast boot and load times, while a larger SATA SSD in the SATA port provides cost-effective game storage capacity, maximizing the available interfaces on the motherboard. Two NVMe SSDs would require two M.2 slots which are unavailable. SATA HDDs would bottleneck game loading compared to SSDs.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.4 — Given a scenario, install and configure motherboards, CPUs, and add-on cards
Question: After installing a new PCIe NIC in a workstation, the existing onboard NIC is no longer available. What BIOS setting likely needs to be checked?
A) Enable virtualization support
B) Disable onboard NIC or set PCIe NIC as primary
C) Enable fast boot
D) Set SATA to AHCI mode
Correct: B
Explanation: Many motherboards automatically disable the onboard NIC when a PCIe NIC is installed, or the BIOS may need to be configured to enable both. Checking the BIOS/UEFI network controller settings allows the technician to re-enable the onboard NIC or configure which adapter is primary. Virtualization, boot speed, and SATA mode settings are unrelated to NIC availability.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.4 — Given a scenario, install and configure motherboards, CPUs, and add-on cards
Question: A technician is installing a CPU and notes the AMD AM4 socket. What socket characteristic describes AM4?
A) LGA — pins on the motherboard socket
B) PGA — pins on the CPU package
C) BGA — permanently soldered to the board
D) ZIF — requires tools to insert the CPU
Correct: B
Explanation: AMD AM4 uses a PGA (Pin Grid Array) design where the pins are on the CPU itself and insert into holes in the motherboard socket, which uses a ZIF (Zero Insertion Force) lever mechanism. Intel's LGA sockets have the pins on the motherboard. BGA packages are soldered and non-removable, used in mobile processors.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.5 — Given a scenario, install or replace the appropriate power supply
Question: A PSU label reads "Input: 100-240V~, 50/60Hz." What does this indicate?
A) The PSU requires a step-down transformer for 240V use
B) The PSU automatically adjusts to both US (110V) and European (220V) power standards
C) The PSU can only be used at 100V
D) The PSU requires manual voltage selection before use
Correct: B
Explanation: A dual-voltage or universal input range of 100-240V indicates the PSU contains auto-sensing circuitry that automatically adjusts to incoming voltage between 100V and 240V at 50 or 60 Hz, making it compatible worldwide without switches or transformers. Older PSUs with fixed-voltage designs require a manual selection switch and are not universal.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.6 — Given a scenario, deploy and configure multifunction devices/printers and settings
Question: A technician installs a new printer on a Windows workstation. The printer uses a manufacturer-specific driver. Why is installing the correct driver important?
A) Drivers determine the printer's physical paper tray capacity
B) Drivers enable communication between the OS and printer hardware, enabling full feature access
C) Drivers set the printer's IP address on the network
D) Drivers physically adjust print head alignment
Correct: B
Explanation: Printer drivers translate OS print commands into the printer's native language (PCL, PostScript, or proprietary), and they expose the printer's features such as duplex, paper type selection, and resolution options to the user and applications. Generic drivers may work for basic printing but will not expose manufacturer-specific features. IP address configuration is done through network settings, not drivers.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.7 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: Which cloud service model requires the least management responsibility from the customer, as the provider handles infrastructure, platform, runtime, and the application itself?
A) IaaS
B) PaaS
C) SaaS
D) DaaS
Correct: C
Explanation: In the SaaS model, the cloud provider manages everything from the physical infrastructure through the application layer; the customer only manages user access and data. IaaS requires the customer to manage OS, middleware, runtime, and applications. PaaS requires management of applications and data.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: A technician identifies an orange fiber optic cable on a patch panel. What type of fiber is this most likely?
A) Single-mode fiber (9/125 µm)
B) Multi-mode OM1 or OM2 fiber (62.5 or 50 µm)
C) Plastic optical fiber (POF)
D) Photonic crystal fiber
Correct: B
Explanation: Orange jacket color is the standard designation for OM1 (62.5 µm) and OM2 (50 µm) multi-mode fiber optic cable. Aqua or blue jackets indicate OM3 and OM4 multi-mode fiber. Single-mode fiber typically uses a yellow jacket. Color-coding helps technicians identify fiber type without testing.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: Which video connector standard supports daisy-chaining multiple monitors from a single output port?
A) HDMI 2.1
B) DVI-D
C) DisplayPort (with MST)
D) VGA
Correct: C
Explanation: DisplayPort supports Multi-Stream Transport (MST), which allows multiple monitors to be daisy-chained from a single DisplayPort output using MST-capable hubs or monitors. HDMI does not support daisy-chaining in consumer implementations. VGA and DVI are single-display analog and digital interfaces respectively.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Given a scenario, install the appropriate RAM
Question: A technician is installing DDR4 RAM but the module will not seat in the slot despite firm pressure. What is the most likely cause?
A) The module is defective
B) The module is being inserted in the wrong direction due to misaligned notch
C) The slot is covered by the CPU cooler
D) DDR4 is incompatible with this motherboard's chipset
Correct: B
Explanation: DDR4 DIMMs have a single notch off-center that acts as a key to ensure correct orientation; if the module is reversed, the notch will not align with the ridge in the slot and it will not seat. Each DDR generation has the notch in a different position to prevent cross-generation installation. A defective module or chipset incompatibility would not cause a physical seating issue.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Given a scenario, select and install storage devices
Question: A home user needs to back up 500 GB of data to removable optical media. Which modern optical disc format can store up to 50 GB per disc and would minimize the number of discs needed?
A) CD-R
B) DVD+R DL
C) BD-R DL (Dual Layer Blu-ray)
D) DVD-R
Correct: C
Explanation: Dual-layer Blu-ray (BD-R DL) can store up to 50 GB per disc, requiring 10 discs to store 500 GB of data. DVD+R DL holds only 8.5 GB per disc, requiring nearly 60 discs. Single-layer Blu-ray holds 25 GB. CDs hold only 700 MB. Blu-ray DL is the most efficient optical backup choice.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.4 — Given a scenario, install and configure motherboards, CPUs, and add-on cards
Question: A Micro-ATX motherboard is being installed in an ATX mid-tower case. Is this compatible?
A) No, Micro-ATX requires a Micro-ATX specific case
B) Yes, ATX cases support Micro-ATX and Mini-ITX boards using the standardized mounting hole positions
C) No, the IO shield will not fit
D) Yes, but an adapter bracket is required
Correct: B
Explanation: ATX cases are designed with mounting holes that accommodate ATX, Micro-ATX, and Mini-ITX motherboards, as all form factors use a common subset of mounting hole positions. The IO shield is motherboard-specific and included with the motherboard, fitting the case's IO cutout. No adapter bracket is needed for this common compatibility.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.4 — Given a scenario, install and configure motherboards, CPUs, and add-on cards
Question: A desktop's CPU temperature consistently reaches 95°C under moderate load. Which corrective action should be performed first?
A) Underclock the CPU in BIOS
B) Replace the thermal paste and reseat the heatsink
C) Add more RAM
D) Replace the power supply
Correct: B
Explanation: Excessive CPU temperatures are most commonly caused by degraded or improperly applied thermal paste creating poor thermal contact between the CPU and heatsink. Reapplying quality thermal paste and ensuring the heatsink is properly seated is the first corrective action. Adding RAM does not affect CPU temperature, and PSU replacement would not resolve thermal issues.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.5 — Given a scenario, install or replace the appropriate power supply
Question: A server farm needs power supplies that can deliver power even when one PSU fails, and the failed unit must be replaceable during operation. What type of PSU configuration is required?
A) High-wattage single PSU
B) 80 Plus Titanium certified PSU
C) Fully modular PSU
D) Hot-swap redundant PSU
Correct: D
Explanation: Hot-swap redundant power supplies allow a failed unit to be removed and a replacement inserted while the system continues running on the remaining PSU(s), critical for server uptime requirements. 80 Plus Titanium is an efficiency rating unrelated to redundancy. Modular cabling reduces clutter but does not provide fault tolerance. A single high-wattage PSU creates a single point of failure.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.6 — Given a scenario, deploy and configure multifunction devices/printers and settings
Question: A user needs to print a brochure with photos at the highest possible print quality. Which setting should be selected in the printer properties?
A) Draft mode
B) Normal quality
C) Economy mode
D) Best or photo quality
Correct: D
Explanation: Best or photo quality settings use the highest resolution DPI (dots per inch) and finer ink application, producing the most detailed output suitable for photographs and professional brochures. Draft and economy modes use less ink and lower resolution for faster, cheaper text printing. Normal quality is a middle ground not optimized for photo output.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.6 — Given a scenario, deploy and configure multifunction devices/printers and settings
Question: An inkjet printer produces output where colors appear shifted, with cyan lines appearing where black text should be. What is the most likely cause?
A) Empty magenta cartridge
B) Misaligned print heads
C) Corrupted printer driver
D) Wrong paper type selected
Correct: B
Explanation: Color shifting and misaligned output in inkjet printers is typically caused by misaligned print heads, which can occur after a cartridge replacement, transport, or mechanical impact. Print head alignment calibration prints a test pattern and adjusts the head positions electronically. Empty cartridges would cause missing color output, not color shifting.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.7 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: A startup wants to avoid capital expenditure on physical servers and instead pay monthly for computing resources that scale with their user growth. Which cloud benefit best describes this model?
A) Resource pooling
B) Rapid elasticity
C) On-demand self-service
D) Metered utilization with pay-as-you-go pricing
Correct: D
Explanation: Metered utilization with pay-as-you-go pricing converts capital expenditure (CapEx) into operating expenditure (OpEx), allowing startups to avoid large upfront hardware investments and pay only for resources consumed. Rapid elasticity is the ability to scale, which complements but is distinct from the billing model. Resource pooling describes shared infrastructure across tenants.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: A gaming enthusiast wants to connect a monitor supporting 8K resolution at 60 Hz. Which cable interface is required?
A) HDMI 1.4
B) DisplayPort 1.2
C) HDMI 2.1
D) DVI-D Dual Link
Correct: C
Explanation: HDMI 2.1 supports up to 10K resolution and 8K at 60 Hz with a maximum bandwidth of 48 Gbps, making it the cable of choice for 8K displays. DisplayPort 1.2 maxes out at 4K/60 Hz in practice. HDMI 1.4 supports only 4K at 30 Hz. DVI-D Dual Link tops out at 2560x1600 at 60 Hz.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: An eSATA cable is used to connect which type of device?
A) An internal 3.5-inch desktop hard drive
B) An external SATA hard drive or SSD enclosure
C) A SCSI tape drive
D) An NVMe external SSD
Correct: B
Explanation: eSATA (External SATA) uses a shielded connector variant of the SATA interface designed for external storage devices such as hard drive enclosures, providing SATA-speed connectivity without the USB overhead. Internal SATA drives use the standard 7-pin SATA connector. NVMe external drives use USB 3.x or Thunderbolt interfaces, not eSATA.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Given a scenario, install the appropriate RAM
Question: A user wants to enable XMP (Extreme Memory Profile) for their DDR4 kit rated at DDR4-3600. What does enabling XMP accomplish?
A) Enables ECC error correction on non-ECC modules
B) Sets the RAM to its rated overclock speed and timings
C) Converts the RAM to dual-channel mode automatically
D) Increases the RAM's voltage to dangerous levels
Correct: B
Explanation: XMP is an Intel specification (AMD calls their version EXPO) that stores overclock profiles on the RAM module's SPD chip; enabling XMP in BIOS applies the manufacturer-validated frequency, timing, and voltage settings for the rated speed. By default, DDR4 runs at JEDEC standard speeds (typically 2133 or 2400 MHz) regardless of the rated speed. XMP does not affect error correction or channel configuration.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Given a scenario, select and install storage devices
Question: A database server requires storage with the lowest possible random read latency for transaction processing. Which storage solution is best?
A) 15,000 RPM SAS HDD
B) SATA SSD
C) NVMe SSD (PCIe Gen 4)
D) RAID 5 array of 7200 RPM HDDs
Correct: C
Explanation: NVMe SSDs on PCIe Gen 4 achieve random read latencies of under 100 microseconds and extremely high IOPS, far exceeding SATA SSDs and spinning disks for database transaction workloads. SATA SSDs offer much better latency than HDDs but are constrained by the SATA interface. RAID 5 with HDDs improves sequential throughput but does not address the inherent rotational latency of spinning disks.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.4 — Given a scenario, install and configure motherboards, CPUs, and add-on cards
Question: A technician is upgrading a CPU. The new processor requires a socket that is different from the existing motherboard socket. What must also be replaced?
A) The RAM modules only
B) The power supply unit
C) The motherboard
D) The GPU
Correct: C
Explanation: CPU sockets are specific to a processor generation and manufacturer; if the new CPU requires a different socket, a new compatible motherboard must be purchased. RAM may also need to be replaced if the new platform requires a different DDR generation. The PSU and GPU are generally not socket-dependent.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.5 — Given a scenario, install or replace the appropriate power supply
Question: Which PSU connector type is used to power PCIe graphics cards and comes in 6-pin and 8-pin variants?
A) EPS CPU connector
B) Molex peripheral connector
C) PCIe power connector
D) SATA power connector
Correct: C
Explanation: PCIe power connectors (6-pin providing 75W and 8-pin providing 150W) are used to supply additional power to discrete graphics cards beyond the 75W available from the PCIe slot itself. The EPS connector powers the CPU. Molex connectors power older peripherals. SATA power connectors power storage devices.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.6 — Given a scenario, deploy and configure multifunction devices/printers and settings
Question: A user needs to send a physical document to a remote office using a multifunction device. The remote office can only receive faxes. Which MFP function should be used?
A) Scan to email
B) Copy
C) Fax
D) Cloud print
Correct: C
Explanation: The fax function on an MFP transmits a scanned document over a telephone line (PSTN or VoIP) to a receiving fax machine or fax server at the remote office. Scan to email requires the recipient to have email capability, not fax. Copy produces a local physical copy. Cloud print sends a job to a networked printer, not to a remote fax machine.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.7 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: A government agency builds a cloud environment exclusively for use by federal agencies with shared security and compliance controls. Which deployment model is this?
A) Public cloud
B) Private cloud
C) Community cloud
D) Hybrid cloud
Correct: C
Explanation: A community cloud is a shared infrastructure built for a specific group of organizations with common requirements such as government security classifications, compliance standards, or regulatory frameworks. It is not open to the general public like a public cloud, and it is not exclusive to a single organization like a private cloud. Multiple government agencies sharing infrastructure is a textbook community cloud.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: A technician measures the attenuation of a fiber optic cable run and finds it exceeds acceptable limits. Which factor most likely caused this?
A) Using Cat 6a instead of Cat 8
B) Excessive bend radius violations in the fiber run
C) Connecting two different RG-6 segments with a barrel connector
D) Running the fiber parallel to power cables
Correct: B
Explanation: Fiber optic cable is sensitive to bending; exceeding the minimum bend radius causes light to escape the core (macrobending loss), significantly increasing signal attenuation. Electromagnetic interference from parallel power cables affects copper cables but not fiber, which is immune to EMI. RG-6 and Cat 6a are copper standards, not fiber.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: USB 4.0 is based on which protocol and achieves a maximum speed of how much?
A) USB 3.2, 20 Gbps
B) Thunderbolt 3, 40 Gbps
C) FireWire 800, 800 Mbps
D) eSATA, 6 Gbps
Correct: B
Explanation: USB 4.0 is based on the Thunderbolt 3 protocol and specification, achieving a maximum speed of 40 Gbps while maintaining backward compatibility with USB 3.2, USB 2.0, and Thunderbolt 3 devices. It uses the USB-C connector exclusively. This integration essentially made Thunderbolt 3 an open standard through USB 4.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Given a scenario, install the appropriate RAM
Question: A technician needs to upgrade the RAM in a Mac Mini with soldered memory. What should the technician advise the user?
A) Replace the logic board with one that has removable RAM
B) The RAM cannot be upgraded as it is permanently attached to the board
C) Install a RAM upgrade kit through the bottom access panel
D) Use an external RAM expansion over Thunderbolt
Correct: B
Explanation: Many modern compact computers, including certain Mac Mini, MacBook, and thin-and-light laptop models, use BGA (Ball Grid Array) soldered RAM that is permanently attached to the logic board and cannot be upgraded. Users must select the desired RAM capacity at the time of purchase. External Thunderbolt RAM expansion devices do not exist as a consumer product.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Given a scenario, select and install storage devices
Question: A field technician installs flash storage into an industrial device that must withstand vibration and shock that would damage spinning drives. Which storage type is most appropriate?
A) 2.5-inch 5400 RPM HDD
B) 3.5-inch 7200 RPM HDD
C) Solid-state flash storage (SSD or eMMC)
D) 10,000 RPM SAS HDD
Correct: C
Explanation: Solid-state storage has no moving parts, making it inherently resistant to vibration and physical shock that would cause read/write head crashes in spinning HDDs. Industrial SSDs and eMMC storage are designed specifically for rugged environments. HDDs at any RPM use mechanical components susceptible to vibration-induced failure.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.4 — Given a scenario, install and configure motherboards, CPUs, and add-on cards
Question: A technician builds a system and the POST completes, but the system will not boot from the new NVMe SSD. The BIOS shows the drive in the storage list. What should be checked next?
A) Replace the NVMe drive
B) Check that the boot order places the NVMe drive first and Secure Boot is compatible
C) Install a SATA SSD instead
D) Update the graphics card driver
Correct: B
Explanation: If the drive is detected but the system won't boot from it, the boot order may have the NVMe drive listed below other bootable devices, or Secure Boot may be rejecting an unsigned bootloader on a freshly installed OS. Setting the NVMe drive first in the boot priority and confirming Secure Boot settings resolves this in most cases. Replacing the drive is premature when it is detected by the BIOS.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.5 — Given a scenario, install or replace the appropriate power supply
Question: A technician measures voltages on a running PSU using a multimeter. The +12V rail reads 11.4V under load. What does this indicate?
A) Normal operation within ATX tolerance
B) PSU is failing — voltage is out of ATX specification
C) The multimeter requires calibration
D) The CPU is overclocked too aggressively
Correct: B
Explanation: The ATX specification allows ±5% tolerance on the +12V rail, meaning acceptable range is 11.4V to 12.6V; however, 11.4V is right at the edge of tolerance and indicates the PSU is struggling under load, a sign of aging or undersized PSU. Voltages consistently below 11.4V are definitively out of specification. This symptom warrants PSU replacement to prevent instability.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.6 — Given a scenario, deploy and configure multifunction devices/printers and settings
Question: A laser printer repeatedly jams at the paper input tray. The paper is the correct size and type. Which component is the most likely cause?
A) Fuser assembly
B) Imaging drum
C) Pickup roller
D) Transfer belt
Correct: C
Explanation: The pickup roller is the rubber roller that grabs paper from the tray and feeds it into the printer; when worn or dirty, it slips and fails to pick up paper consistently, causing paper jams at the input. The fuser is located at the output end and causes jams or smearing there. The imaging drum and transfer belt are involved in toner application, not paper feeding.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.7 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: An organization's IT team manages virtual machines on cloud infrastructure but the cloud provider manages the physical servers, networking, and storage hardware. Which cloud model is the organization using?
A) SaaS
B) PaaS
C) IaaS
D) On-premises
Correct: C
Explanation: In the IaaS model, the cloud provider owns and manages the physical infrastructure (servers, network, storage) while the customer is responsible for the virtual machines, OS, middleware, runtime, applications, and data running on that infrastructure. SaaS manages everything including the application. PaaS manages up through the runtime, leaving only application and data to the customer.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: A technician needs to cable a rack of servers to a top-of-rack switch using very short high-speed copper links. Which cable type is specifically designed for this use case?
A) Cat 6a patch cables
B) Direct Attach Copper (DAC) cables with SFP+ connectors
C) Multi-mode fiber with LC connectors
D) eSATA cables
Correct: B
Explanation: Direct Attach Copper (DAC) cables with SFP+ or QSFP connectors are passive copper cables used for very short (1-7 meter) server-to-switch connections in data centers, providing 10, 25, or 40 Gbps connectivity at lower cost than fiber optic solutions. Cat 6a supports 10 Gbps at 100 meters but uses RJ-45 connectors incompatible with SFP ports. DAC cables are the standard short-range data center interconnect.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Given a scenario, install the appropriate RAM
Question: Which characteristic distinguishes DDR5 from DDR4 in terms of on-module design?
A) DDR5 uses a 288-pin connector identical to DDR4
B) DDR5 integrates a power management IC (PMIC) directly on the module
C) DDR5 requires a higher 1.5V operating voltage
D) DDR5 uses a 240-pin connector for backward compatibility
Correct: B
Explanation: DDR5 moves the voltage regulator circuitry onto the module itself as a PMIC (Power Management Integrated Circuit), shifting power regulation from the motherboard to each DIMM for better stability and more precise voltage control. DDR5 uses 288 pins but with a different notch position than DDR4, preventing cross-installation. DDR5 operates at 1.1V, lower than DDR4's 1.2V.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Given a scenario, select and install storage devices
Question: A technician configures a RAID 1 array with two 4 TB drives. What is the total usable storage capacity?
A) 8 TB
B) 6 TB
C) 4 TB
D) 2 TB
Correct: C
Explanation: RAID 1 mirrors the same data on both drives, providing fault tolerance but using only half the total raw capacity for usable storage. With two 4 TB drives (8 TB raw), only 4 TB is usable. The remaining 4 TB is used for the redundant mirror copy. RAID 0 would yield 8 TB usable but with no redundancy.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.4 — Given a scenario, install and configure motherboards, CPUs, and add-on cards
Question: A technician replaces a CPU cooler. When removing the old heatsink, the CPU comes out of the socket attached to the heatsink. Which type of socket does this system use?
A) LGA (Land Grid Array)
B) BGA (Ball Grid Array)
C) ZIF (Zero Insertion Force) — PGA
D) FCLGA (Flip Chip LGA)
Correct: C
Explanation: In PGA (Pin Grid Array) sockets used by AMD, the CPU has pins that insert into the socket; if thermal paste has become adhesive over time, the CPU can lift out of the socket attached to the heatsink rather than remaining in the socket. LGA sockets (used by Intel) have the pins on the socket, and the CPU typically stays on the motherboard since there are no pins to pull it up. ZIF is the lever mechanism used with PGA sockets.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.6 — Given a scenario, deploy and configure multifunction devices/printers and settings
Question: A user reports their wireless printer disconnects frequently and must be reconnected manually. The printer is near the router. What is the most effective long-term solution?
A) Reinstall the printer driver weekly
B) Assign the printer a static IP or DHCP reservation and ensure the wireless signal is on a consistent channel
C) Move the printer to a USB connection on a nearby workstation
D) Replace the printer's ink cartridges
Correct: B
Explanation: Wireless printer disconnections are often caused by IP address changes (DHCP lease expiration) or wireless channel interference causing the connection to drop. Assigning a static IP or DHCP reservation ensures the printer's address doesn't change, while optimizing wireless channel reduces interference-related drops. USB connection is a workaround that eliminates wireless functionality. Ink cartridges are unrelated to network connectivity.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.7 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: Which cloud characteristic means services are available to users over the network and accessible through standard client devices such as laptops, tablets, and smartphones?
A) Resource pooling
B) Rapid elasticity
C) Broad network access
D) Measured service
Correct: C
Explanation: Broad network access means cloud services are accessible over the network using standard mechanisms, available on diverse client platforms (thin clients, laptops, smartphones) without requiring specialized hardware. Resource pooling refers to shared physical infrastructure. Rapid elasticity refers to scalability. Measured service refers to pay-per-use billing.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Explain basic cable types and their connectors, features, and purposes
Question: A network engineer is troubleshooting a Cat 6a cable installation rated for 10GBase-T. The cable runs 95 meters and includes 3 meters of patch cable at each end. What concern should the engineer have?
A) None; the total run is well within the 100-meter limit
B) The combined length of 101 meters exceeds the 100-meter channel limit, potentially causing errors
C) Cat 6a cannot support 10GBase-T; Cat 7 is required
D) Patch cables must be Cat 8 to maintain 10GBase-T certification
Correct: B
Explanation: The 100-meter channel limit for 10GBase-T includes all cable segments (horizontal run plus patch cables at both ends). A 95-meter horizontal run plus 3 meters at each end equals 101 meters total, technically exceeding the specification. The engineer should shorten the horizontal run or use shorter patch cables to stay within 100 meters total. Cat 6a fully supports 10GBase-T.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.4 — Given a scenario, install and configure motherboards, CPUs, and add-on cards
Question: Which expansion card type would a technician install to add 10 Gigabit Ethernet connectivity to a workstation that only has a 1 Gigabit onboard NIC?
A) Sound card
B) 10GbE NIC (Network Interface Card)
C) RAID controller card
D) Video capture card
Correct: B
Explanation: A 10 Gigabit Ethernet NIC installed in a PCIe slot provides the 10GbE port needed for high-bandwidth network connectivity, replacing or supplementing the onboard 1GbE NIC. Sound cards add audio processing capability. RAID controllers add storage interface functionality. Video capture cards handle external video input.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.5 — Given a scenario, install or replace the appropriate power supply
Question: A small form factor (SFF) desktop uses a TFX-style power supply rather than a standard ATX PSU. A technician needs to replace it. What must they consider?
A) TFX PSUs use different voltage rails than ATX PSUs
B) TFX PSUs have the same form factor as ATX and are interchangeable
C) The replacement must be a TFX form factor to fit the SFF case
D) TFX PSUs only support up to 250W output
Correct: C
Explanation: TFX (Thin Form Factor) power supplies have a specific smaller physical footprint designed for SFF cases; the replacement must match the TFX form factor to physically fit. TFX PSUs use the same ATX connector specifications and voltage rails as standard ATX PSUs. TFX PSUs are available in various wattage ratings, not limited to 250W.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Given a scenario, select and install storage devices
Question: A system builder installs a new M.2 NVMe SSD and a SATA SSD simultaneously. After installation, only the SATA SSD appears in the BIOS. What is most likely the cause?
A) The NVMe SSD is defective
B) The M.2 slot shares lanes with a SATA port and enabling both creates a conflict
C) NVMe SSDs require a device driver installed before the BIOS can detect them
D) SATA and NVMe cannot coexist in the same system
Correct: B
Explanation: On many consumer motherboards, the M.2 slot shares PCIe or SATA lanes with physical SATA ports; enabling both devices simultaneously can cause a conflict where the motherboard disables one interface. The motherboard manual documents which SATA ports are disabled when the M.2 slot is populated. Drivers are not required for BIOS-level drive detection, and SATA/NVMe coexistence is normally supported if lane conflicts are avoided.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.6 — Given a scenario, deploy and configure multifunction devices/printers and settings
Question: A user needs to print a confidential document and wants to ensure it is not printed until they authenticate at the printer. Which feature provides this capability?
A) Cloud printing
B) Secure/PIN printing (pull printing)
C) Duplex printing
D) Collation
Correct: B
Explanation: Secure printing (also called PIN printing or pull printing) holds the print job in the printer's memory queue until the user enters a PIN or authenticates at the printer's control panel, preventing sensitive documents from sitting unattended in the output tray. Cloud printing sends jobs to a remote print queue. Duplex and collation are output formatting features.

Domain: 3.0 Hardware
Sub-objective: 3.7 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: An organization wants to migrate some workloads to the cloud while keeping others on-premises due to data sovereignty requirements. Which cloud model enables this?
A) Public cloud only
B) SaaS
C) Hybrid cloud
D) Community cloud
Correct: C
Explanation: A hybrid cloud integrates on-premises infrastructure with public or private cloud resources, allowing the organization to keep sensitive data on-premises for compliance or data sovereignty reasons while leveraging cloud scalability for other workloads. A pure public cloud model would move all workloads off-premises. Community cloud is shared among organizations with common concerns rather than a mix of on-prem and cloud.
Domain: 4.0 Virtualization and Cloud Computing
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: Which cloud service model provides customers with virtualized computing infrastructure such as servers, storage, and networking, but requires the customer to manage the operating system and applications?
A) SaaS
B) PaaS
C) IaaS
D) DaaS
Correct: C
Explanation: Infrastructure as a Service (IaaS) gives customers access to virtualized hardware resources like compute, storage, and networking over the internet. The cloud provider manages the physical infrastructure, while the customer is responsible for the OS, middleware, and applications. Examples include Amazon EC2 and Microsoft Azure Virtual Machines.

Domain: 4.0 Virtualization and Cloud Computing
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: A developer needs a platform to build, test, and deploy applications without managing the underlying servers or runtime environments. Which cloud model best fits this need?
A) IaaS
B) PaaS
C) SaaS
D) Private cloud
Correct: B
Explanation: Platform as a Service (PaaS) provides a managed environment for developers to build and deploy applications without worrying about the underlying infrastructure or runtime. The cloud provider manages the OS, middleware, and runtime, while the developer focuses on writing code. Google App Engine and Microsoft Azure App Service are common PaaS examples.

Domain: 4.0 Virtualization and Cloud Computing
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: A company uses Microsoft 365 for email and document collaboration. Employees access it through a web browser without installing software locally. Which cloud service model is this?
A) IaaS
B) PaaS
C) DaaS
D) SaaS
Correct: D
Explanation: Software as a Service (SaaS) delivers fully functional applications over the internet, managed entirely by the cloud provider. Users access the software through a browser or thin client, with no local installation required. Microsoft 365, Google Workspace, and Salesforce are well-known SaaS examples.

Domain: 4.0 Virtualization and Cloud Computing
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: Which cloud deployment model is owned and operated exclusively by a single organization and hosted either on-premises or by a third party?
A) Public cloud
B) Community cloud
C) Hybrid cloud
D) Private cloud
Correct: D
Explanation: A private cloud is dedicated to a single organization, providing greater control, security, and customization compared to public cloud options. It can be hosted on the organization's own data center or managed by a third-party provider. Private clouds are commonly used by enterprises with strict regulatory or security requirements.

Domain: 4.0 Virtualization and Cloud Computing
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: A hospital network shares a cloud environment with other healthcare organizations to comply with HIPAA regulations while sharing costs. Which cloud deployment model describes this arrangement?
A) Public cloud
B) Hybrid cloud
C) Community cloud
D) Private cloud
Correct: C
Explanation: A community cloud is shared among several organizations with common concerns such as regulatory requirements, security standards, or mission goals. The infrastructure and costs are shared between the participating organizations, which reduces expense while maintaining a level of exclusivity. Healthcare, government, and financial sectors commonly use community cloud models.

Domain: 4.0 Virtualization and Cloud Computing
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: A retail company keeps sensitive customer data in its private cloud but uses a public cloud for its customer-facing website during peak shopping seasons. Which deployment model is the company using?
A) Community cloud
B) Hybrid cloud
C) Multi-cloud
D) Private cloud
Correct: B
Explanation: A hybrid cloud combines private and public cloud environments, allowing data and applications to move between them as needed. This model gives organizations flexibility to keep sensitive workloads on-premises or in a private cloud while bursting to public cloud for scalability. It balances control, security, and cost-effectiveness.

Domain: 4.0 Virtualization and Cloud Computing
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: Which cloud characteristic allows a provider to automatically scale resources up or down in response to fluctuating demand without human intervention?
A) Metered utilization
B) Resource pooling
C) Rapid elasticity
D) On-demand self-service
Correct: C
Explanation: Rapid elasticity is the ability of a cloud environment to quickly scale resources up or down to meet changing demand, often automatically. This ensures applications have the capacity they need during peak loads without over-provisioning. It is one of the five essential NIST characteristics of cloud computing.

Domain: 4.0 Virtualization and Cloud Computing
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: A cloud provider charges customers only for the compute hours, storage space, and data transfer they actually consume each month. Which cloud characteristic does this describe?
A) Rapid elasticity
B) Resource pooling
C) On-demand self-service
D) Metered utilization
Correct: D
Explanation: Metered utilization (also called measured service) means cloud resources are monitored, controlled, and reported, and customers are billed only for what they consume. This pay-as-you-go model is analogous to a utility bill for electricity or water. It allows organizations to align IT costs directly with actual usage.

Domain: 4.0 Virtualization and Cloud Computing
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: Which cloud characteristic allows a single pool of physical resources such as CPU, memory, and storage to be dynamically allocated among multiple tenants?
A) Metered utilization
B) Resource pooling
C) Rapid elasticity
D) Measured service
Correct: B
Explanation: Resource pooling means the provider's physical and virtual resources are pooled together and dynamically assigned to multiple consumers based on demand. Customers generally have no control or knowledge over the exact location of those physical resources. This multi-tenant model enables efficient utilization of infrastructure across many customers.

Domain: 4.0 Virtualization and Cloud Computing
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: A user provisions a new virtual machine on AWS through a web console without calling or emailing the cloud provider. Which cloud characteristic is being demonstrated?
A) Rapid elasticity
B) Resource pooling
C) On-demand self-service
D) Broad network access
Correct: C
Explanation: On-demand self-service allows consumers to unilaterally provision computing capabilities as needed, automatically and without requiring human interaction with the service provider. This capability empowers users to spin up or tear down resources instantly through a portal or API. It is a core NIST characteristic of cloud computing.

Domain: 4.0 Virtualization and Cloud Computing
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: An organization migrates its on-premises email server to a hosted cloud service managed entirely by a third-party provider. What term best describes this cloud-based email solution?
A) Virtual desktop
B) Off-site email
C) SaaS desktop
D) PaaS messaging
Correct: B
Explanation: Off-site email refers to hosted email services where the mail server infrastructure is managed by a cloud provider rather than the organization's own IT department. Services like Microsoft Exchange Online or Google Workspace Gmail are examples of off-site email. This reduces the burden of server maintenance, patching, and backup on the organization.

Domain: 4.0 Virtualization and Cloud Computing
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: Which cloud service allows users to store, sync, and share files from any device via the internet, replacing local file servers?
A) Virtual desktop infrastructure
B) Application streaming
C) Cloud file storage
D) Community cloud
Correct: C
Explanation: Cloud file storage services such as Dropbox, Google Drive, and OneDrive allow users to store files remotely and access them from any internet-connected device. Files are synchronized across devices and can be shared with others easily. This eliminates dependence on local file servers and simplifies collaboration.

Domain: 4.0 Virtualization and Cloud Computing
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: A company wants to provide employees with a full Windows desktop environment accessible from any device, including thin clients and tablets. Which cloud solution should the company deploy?
A) SaaS email
B) Virtual desktop infrastructure
C) Application streaming
D) IaaS storage
Correct: B
Explanation: Virtual Desktop Infrastructure (VDI) hosts desktop operating systems and applications on centralized servers in the cloud or data center, delivering the desktop experience to end users over a network. Users can access their desktops from thin clients, tablets, or any browser-capable device. This simplifies endpoint management and improves security by keeping data centralized.

Domain: 4.0 Virtualization and Cloud Computing
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: An employee opens a CAD application on a low-powered Chromebook. The application runs on a remote server and only the display output is sent to the local device. Which technology is being used?
A) Type 1 hypervisor
B) Cloud file storage
C) Virtual application streaming
D) Resource pooling
Correct: C
Explanation: Virtual application streaming (app streaming) delivers applications from a remote server to a client device, executing the application server-side while sending only the visual output to the client. This allows resource-intensive software to run on lightweight hardware. Citrix Virtual Apps and VMware Horizon Apps are well-known examples.

Domain: 4.0 Virtualization and Cloud Computing
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: Which of the following is the BEST example of a public cloud service?
A) A company's internal server room running VMware ESXi
B) Amazon Web Services providing compute resources to any paying customer
C) A government agency sharing a cloud with other federal departments
D) A hospital running its own virtualized infrastructure
Correct: B
Explanation: A public cloud is owned and operated by a third-party provider that makes resources available to any individual or organization over the internet. Amazon Web Services (AWS), Microsoft Azure, and Google Cloud Platform are leading public cloud providers. Public clouds offer high scalability and a pay-as-you-go pricing model.

Domain: 4.0 Virtualization and Cloud Computing
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: A company's cloud contract specifies that resource usage is logged, and the company is billed based on exact consumption of CPU, storage, and bandwidth. Which NIST cloud characteristic does this represent?
A) On-demand self-service
B) Broad network access
C) Measured service
D) Rapid elasticity
Correct: C
Explanation: Measured service (closely related to metered utilization) means cloud systems automatically control and optimize resource use through metering. Usage data is transparently available to both the provider and the consumer for billing and monitoring purposes. This promotes accountability and cost control in cloud environments.

Domain: 4.0 Virtualization and Cloud Computing
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: Which cloud deployment model would MOST likely be chosen by a small business that wants the lowest cost and does not have sensitive compliance requirements?
A) Private cloud
B) Community cloud
C) Hybrid cloud
D) Public cloud
Correct: D
Explanation: Public cloud is the most cost-effective option because infrastructure costs are shared among many customers and there is no capital expenditure for hardware. Small businesses without strict regulatory requirements benefit from the flexibility and scalability of public cloud services. Providers manage all maintenance, security patching, and hardware refreshes.

Domain: 4.0 Virtualization and Cloud Computing
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Summarize cloud-computing concepts
Question: A technician is explaining that multiple customers share the same underlying physical hardware in a cloud data center, but each customer's data and workloads are logically isolated. Which cloud concept is the technician describing?
A) Rapid elasticity
B) Multi-tenancy and resource pooling
C) On-demand self-service
D) Virtual desktop infrastructure
Correct: B
Explanation: Multi-tenancy is a fundamental cloud concept where multiple customers (tenants) share the same physical infrastructure while remaining logically isolated from each other. Resource pooling supports this by dynamically allocating shared hardware resources to different tenants as needed. Proper isolation mechanisms ensure that one tenant cannot access another's data.

Domain: 4.0 Virtualization and Cloud Computing
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Summarize aspects of client-side virtualization
Question: Which of the following BEST describes the primary purpose of a virtual machine (VM)?
A) To replace physical network switches with software-defined alternatives
B) To run multiple isolated operating system instances on a single physical host
C) To stream applications from a remote server to a thin client
D) To provide encrypted tunnels between remote offices
Correct: B
Explanation: A virtual machine is a software-based emulation of a physical computer that runs its own operating system and applications in an isolated environment.
